# Deferred-Anchor Registry

> The canonical source of truth for every `D-*` anchor cited in `src/` but
> deferred to a future cycle. The leading underscore sorts this file before
> the numbered plans in directory listings — call this out as the registry,
> not a plan. Per-plan §3.1 rows are still the preferred home for anchors
> whose feature area maps cleanly onto a plan; this file catches the orphans
> + cross-cutting anchors that don't belong to any single plan.
>
> **CI/pre-commit guard** (`tools/check-anchor-registry.{sh,ps1}`): every
> `D-*` identifier appearing in `src/` MUST resolve to a row in this file
> OR a citation in any `.plans/*.md`. Pre-fix this recurred TWICE
> (memory: "the same gap silent-failure caught for MULTI-PAGE-GOT").
> The guard makes the system enforce the discipline — same shape as the
> agnosticism veto + the `CallConv` static_assert.
>
> **V2-4.X / full-C ownership (2026-06-10):** the C-language-feature deferral
> CLUSTER — modulo codegen (`D-CSUBSET-MOD-OP-CODEGEN`, …), primitive widths
> (`D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH`), linkage/visibility syntax
> (`D-CSUBSET-LINKAGE-VISIBILITY-SYNTAX`, `D-DECL-PREFIX-STRIP-SHARED-HELPER`),
> rodata aggregates (`D-LK4-RODATA-PRODUCER-NONSTRING-ARRAY`), non-main implicit
> return (`D-LK10-ENTRY-MAIN-IMPLICIT-RETURN` — the OPEN non-main successor row,
> cross-ref `D-CSUBSET-ENTRY-NAME-SPLIT`), variadic FFI
> (`D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE`), the apple-arm64 ABI divergence
> (`D-FF3-APPLE-ARM64-ABI-DIVERGENCE`), and peers — is now OWNED by **stepper
> V2-4.X / [`23-full-c-plan`](./23-full-c-plan%20-%20tbd.md)** (c-subset → full
> C23). Each closes inside the relevant FC phase (see the plan §3.1).
>
> **NOT in this cluster — already shipped, do NOT re-claim as new FC work**
> (caught by the 2026-06-10 plan-lock accuracy review). Two genuinely-CLOSED
> anchors: `D-CSUBSET-DIVISION-OP-CODEGEN` (✅ 2026-06-04 — signed division shipped;
> the modulo successor `D-CSUBSET-MOD-OP-CODEGEN` ✅ since closed too — FC1 cycle 1, 2026-06-10, above) and `D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH`
> (✅ 2026-06-08 — direct-plt/indirect-slot dispatch shipped; the OPEN variadic concern
> is `D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE`, above). PLUS one closed FEATURE with no
> anchor row: the `main` implicit-return-0 (shipped 2026-06-02, live in
> `c-subset.lang.json`, config-only) — the anchor `D-LK10-ENTRY-MAIN-IMPLICIT-RETURN`
> itself remains the still-OPEN non-main successor (above), NOT a closed item. The
> full-C arc supersedes each predecessor with its named successor, never by reopening it.
>
> New full-C exotic-tail exclusions land as `D-FULLC-*` rows as clusters ship.
> Individual rows are NOT rewritten here yet (the plan is the live map until a
> cycle actually closes the anchor).
>
> **Schema (one row per anchor)**:
> ```
> | Anchor | Trigger | Closing work | Cross-refs |
> ```
>
> When an anchor closes, replace its row's status with `✅ CLOSED <date>`
> and cite the commit/SymbolId. Don't delete the row — the audit trail is
> load-bearing for future regressions.
>
> **Authorization log — robustness sweep (2026-06-24, branch `feature/0-0-2-p14`):**
> the user authorized a "robustness sweep," which FIRED the trigger for three
> trigger-gated anchors and CLOSED them in one sweep (393/393 ctest, MSVC
> Release + MinGW): `D-CSUBSET-BLOCK-SCOPE-PROTOTYPE`,
> `D-CSUBSET-EXTERN-DEFINITION-MERGE`, and
> `D-SEMANTIC-ASSIGN-STMT-ASSIGNABILITY-BYPASS` (see their rows below). The
> sweep surfaced one new backlog row, `D-CSUBSET-TENTATIVE-DEFINITION-MERGE`
> (C 6.9.2 tentative definitions — still fail-loud, trigger-gated).

## Anchor Index

| Anchor | Trigger | Closing work | Cross-refs |
|---|---|---|---|
| `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD` | ✅ **GUARD DELIVERED 2026-06-20 (FC13 hardening cycle); CAP RAISED 16→256 on 2026-06-20 (FC13 cycle 2) once both cap-raise blockers (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` + `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`) closed — the cap is now a real SEMANTIC limit, not a host-stack artifact (parse is O(N) + the frontend's deep recursion [CU build + `analyze`] runs on a 64 MiB worker stack via `core/substrate/large_stack_call`). The "lowered to 16" note below is HISTORICAL.** The Pratt-walker expression-depth guard (`ParserConfig::maxExpressionDepth`, enforced at the single chokepoint `parseExpressionAt` in `src/analysis/syntactic/parser.cpp`) was a `fatal()`/`std::abort()` on overflow, and its cap (256) was ~10x too high for the host C++ stack: the heaviest path (the paren atom re-entry `parsePrimary->parseUntilFrameDepth->stepOnce->walkExpression->parseExpressionAt`) overflows a Windows ~1 MB Debug stack at depth ~25 — BEFORE the guard could fire — so deeply-nested input RAW-crashed (rc 127) or hung. **DELIVERED:** (1) the `fatal()` is now a POSITIONED `P_ExpressionTooDeep` (0x0018) at the offending token + graceful RECOVERY (`recoverExpressionTooDeep_`: emit-once + Error leaf via `panicRecover` + unwind), never an abort/overflow; (2) the default cap lowered 256→16 so the guard fires with comfortable margin below the Debug paren overflow (~25) while still admitting realistic hand-written C nesting (≤15 deep). STEP-1 empirical finding: (B) on-path (NOT a bypass) — `expressionDepth` DOES grow per nesting level; the cap was simply unreachable before the stack blew. **CAP-RAISE follow-up → `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`:** EXPLORED this cycle and found INSUFFICIENT — a parser-only large-stack worker thread does NOT enable a higher cap, because stage markers localized the ~25-level overflow DOWNSTREAM of the parser (semantic `analyze` / HIR-MIR lowering recurse over the expr tree on the host's MAIN ~1 MB stack); raising the cap needs the downstream stages deep-safe (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`) AND the speculative cost bounded (`D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`). **SECOND follow-up (distinct, pre-existing) — c-subset speculative-operand O(N²):** the depth guard eliminates the CRASH, but on PATHOLOGICALLY deep parens the c-subset full parse is SLOW (CLI @ cap=16: depth 100 ~2s, 150-200 ~12s, 250+ >25s) because the `operand` rule is `speculative:true` (compoundLiteral/cast/paren disambiguation, lookahead 64 = 1024-token probe budget): each of the cap-many paren levels re-probes the deep tail, and nested speculation (`maxSpeculationDepth=8`) rollback-re-parses it. This is INDEPENDENT of the cap (cap=8 still times out @ depth 1000) and of THIS fix (pre-fix the deep parens crashed in Pratt recursion before the speculation finished; the fix EXPOSES the speculation cost, it does not cause it). A NON-speculative grammar (`kParenSchema`) parses 1000 parens in ~10ms — the headline unit test pins exactly that (the GUARD mechanism, isolated from c-subset speculation). The fix is a speculation-engine / grammar concern (memoize probe results, or bound speculation by expression depth), NOT the depth guard. Note: only manifests on ALREADY-INVALID input (depth > cap); valid C nests ≤4 in the entire corpus. Tests: `PrattWalker.{ExceedingMaxExpressionDepthDiagnosesAndRecovers (lowered-cap structural pin), DeeplyNestedParensDiagnoseAtDefaultCapWithoutCrashing (1000 parens @ default cap → positioned diag, no rc-127), DeepPrefixChainDiagnosesAndRecovers, DeepTernaryChainDiagnosesAndRecovers}` (test_pratt_walker.cpp) PLUS the c-subset end-to-end golden pin `tests/corpus/diagnostics/c-subset/expression_too_deeply_nested.c` (real frontend → `P_ExpressionTooDeep 1:41-1:42` golden, the exact code+position at the 17th paren where cap=16 trips). | (guard delivered; cap-raise → the 2 dedicated anchors) | plan 05 (PA2 walker); `D-PP-FATAL-HALTS-PARSE` (sibling); `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` + `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` |
| `D-PP-FATAL-HALTS-PARSE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 (FC13 hardening cycle).** The compilation-unit PP branch (`compilation_unit.cpp` `parseAndAdd_`) parsed UNCONDITIONALLY even when a FATAL preprocessor backstop had TRUNCATED the synthesized stream (the >256 macro-expansion-nesting guard or the include-nesting guard), feeding the truncated tokens to the parser — producing an inscrutable secondary cascade / hang on top of the real PP cause. **CLOSED:** added `PreprocessResult::fatal` (set ONLY by the two stream-TRUNCATING backstops: `MacroExpander::truncated_` at the >256 guard, `SynthBuilder::fatal` ref-threaded through the recursive include builders at the include-depth guard); the CU gate now keys on `pp.fatal` and, when true, feeds the parser an EOF-ONLY stream — yielding a minimal well-formed tree that STILL carries the (remapped) PP diagnostics, halting the parse before the cascade. Crucially the gate is NARROW: a RECOVERABLE PP error (missing `#include` file, malformed directive, redefinition) or a folded LEXER error leaves the stream INTACT and the parser STILL runs (an earlier `diagnostics->hasErrors()` gate was too broad — it swallowed the rest of a file on an unresolved `#include`; caught by `HirLoweringCSubset.IncludeDirectiveIsSkippedNotFailed` + the FFI ingest tests). Tests: `CompilationUnitPPGate.{FatalMacroNestingTruncationGatesParser, OrdinaryMacroCompileIsNotGated, UnresolvedIncludeStillParsesRestOfFile}` (test_compilation_unit.cpp). | (closed) | `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD` (sibling); plan 05; FC13 |
| `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 (FC13 cycle 2 — deep-expression-nesting end-to-end).** Built the standard compiler facility for deep recursion: `src/core/substrate/large_stack_call.{hpp,cpp}` — `runOnLargeStack(stackBytes, fn)` runs `fn` on a dedicated worker thread with a `stackBytes`-RESERVE stack, JOINs (synchronous — no concurrency), and re-throws any exception `fn` threw (captured into `std::exception_ptr` on the worker, rethrown on the joiner; never escapes the entry → no `std::terminate`); value-returning convenience `callOnLargeStack`; `kDeepRecursionStackBytes = 64 MiB` (cap 256 × ~40 KB/level ≈ 10 MB, lazily-committed reserve costs ~nothing). FAIL-LOUD (`std::abort` + stderr) on every thread-API failure AND caller bug (empty `fn`, `stackBytes==0`, Windows `stackBytes > UINT_MAX` — reject, never truncate the 32-bit `_beginthreadex` arg). Windows arm = `_beginthreadex` + `STACK_SIZE_PARAM_IS_A_RESERVATION` + `WaitForSingleObject`/`CloseHandle`; POSIX arm = `pthread_attr_setstacksize`/`pthread_create`/`pthread_join` (CI-verified — no `find_package(Threads)`, raw symbols resolve as `std::thread`'s do). AGNOSTIC: pure host/OS utility, names no language/CPU/format; the `_WIN32`/POSIX `#ifdef` is host-portability. Self-test `tests/core/substrate/test_large_stack_call.cpp` (RunsTheCallable; RethrowsEscapedException value-preserving; ProvidesStackForDeepRecursion = ~1000 frames × `volatile char[8192]` ≈ 8 MB that the default stack can't hold). **KEY EMPIRICAL CORRECTION of the localization below:** wrapping JUST `analyze` was INSUFFICIENT — stage markers in the full c-subset→PE-exec pipeline showed the analyze-wrap lifted the DOWNSTREAM ceiling well past 25 (n=100..180 compile + run clean), but at the raised cap (256) a NEW overflow appeared UPSTREAM: the **CU build (parse / preprocess / type-name oracle)** in `Program::compileFiles`/`compileUnits` (`UnitBuilder::addFile`→`finish`) recurses building the expression tree and overflows the host main stack at ~n=185 (Debug-MSVC) — the low cap (16) had MASKED it (the guard fired at 16, no deep tree was ever built). So the CU build, `analyze`, AND the BUILD-half `buildCuMir` (HIR + MIR) are ALL wrapped on the 64 MiB stack: `analyze` via a file-static `analyzeImpl` + a thin public `analyze` (`callOnLargeStack(kDeepRecursionStackBytes, …)`); the two CU-build sites in `program.cpp` via `callOnLargeStack` returning the `CompilationUnit`. The BUILD half `buildCuMir` (= analyze + CST->HIR + HIR->MIR) is wrapped via a file-static `buildCuMirImpl` + a thin `buildCuMir` (`compile_pipeline.cpp`). **THIRD incompleteness, independent-audit-caught (this cycle's dss-audit):** wrapping JUST parse + analyze was STILL insufficient — CST->HIR (`cst_to_hir.cpp` `lowerExpr`/`lowerOperand`) and HIR->MIR (`hir_to_mir.cpp` `lowerExpr`) ALSO recurse one host-stack frame per nesting level, running inline on the MAIN thread inside `buildCuMir` AFTER `analyze`'s worker has joined; so a valid 41..256-deep expression that parsed + analyzed could still overflow downstream (it HAPPENED to fit at n<=250 on Debug-MSVC, but that is host/frame-size luck, NOT a guarantee — exactly the uncontrolled-margin the wrap removes). FIXED by the `buildCuMir` wrap (analyze nests as a benign inner worker; peak live-deep stack ~10 MB << 64 MiB). Only the LOWER half (MIR->LIR->codegen->link, `lowerMirModuleToAssembly`) genuinely needs no wrap — it iterates a FLAT SSA arena (`mir.hpp`), NOT a tree, so it is non-recursive in nesting depth (audit-confirmed). Cap raised 16→**256** (`parser.hpp`); now a real SEMANTIC limit (parse O(N) via `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`'s LL(k) prune + analyze/parse on the big stack), so deep-but-legal C compiles end-to-end and only pathological nesting past 256 trips the positioned `P_ExpressionTooDeep` guard. **Verified:** n=100/200/250 c-subset compile (rc 0, ~0.2s) + run (exit 0); n=300 fails LOUD fast (`P0018`, no hang/crash). Test harnesses that build deep CUs unwrapped were also routed onto the facility (the corpus harness `test_diagnostic_corpus.cpp` for the >256-paren fixture; the headline `PrattWalker.DeeplyNestedParensDiagnoseAtDefaultCapWithoutCrashing` 1000-paren pin at the raised default cap) and the duplicate local `runOnLargeStack` in `test_parser_speculation.cpp` was CONSOLIDATED onto the substrate facility (Win32 `CreateThread` trampoline deleted). Re-added + DEEPENED the runnable witness `examples/c-subset/deeply_nested_expression` (200 nested parens → exit 7; PE-windows + ELF-linux) — a VALID deep expression that compiles AND runs through the WHOLE BUILD+LOWER pipeline at 200 nesting levels (closes the audit's M2: the prior 40-paren example + the guard-tripping fixtures never lowered a valid deep tree past HIR). Corpus fixture `expression_too_deeply_nested.c` regenerated to 300 parens (golden `P_ExpressionTooDeep 1:281-1:282` + `P_UnexpectedToken 1:582-1:583`). 335 ctest green. — *Original localization (audit trail):* Frontend stages DOWNSTREAM of the parser (semantic `analyze`, HIR/MIR lowering) recurse over the expression tree on the host's MAIN ~1 MB stack (Windows) and OVERFLOW at ~25 nested levels (rc-127, NO diagnostic), independent of the parser (which handles deeper). This is what caps `ParserConfig::maxExpressionDepth` at 16. Localized empirically via stage markers in `program.cpp` `runCusToTargets` (parse completes; the crash is inside `compileOneTarget`→`analyze`). A parser-only large-stack worker thread was EXPLORED this cycle and does NOT help (the crash is downstream). [SUPERSEDED: the crash was ALSO upstream in the CU build once the cap allowed a deep tree — see the close note above.] | (closed — `large_stack_call` substrate; CU build + `analyze` + BUILD-half `buildCuMir` [HIR/MIR] on a 64 MiB worker stack; cap 16→256) | `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD`; `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`; `parser.hpp` maxExpressionDepth; `core/substrate/large_stack_call.hpp` |
| `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 — fixed by a config-driven LL(k) predictive prune (the `Correct direction (b)` below, IMPLEMENTED): `computePredictivePrefixes` (grammar_schema_json.cpp) precomputes a per-rule FIRST_k `predictivePrefix` at schema-load (the leading single-token run + the first variable element's FIRST set, STOPPING before a NULLABLE stop element so each recorded offset is an EXACT admissible-token set ⇒ a SOUND over-approximation); `predictivePrefixPrunes` (parser.cpp) prunes a speculative candidate when an OBSERVED next-token is outside its prefix; a lone unguarded survivor DESCENDS DIRECTLY (no probe). `((` → castExpr/compoundLiteral pruned (token[+1]=`(` ∉ FIRST(castTypeRef)) ⇒ O(N); n=300 154s→0.17s (~1100×); the lone-`(Identifier)` ambiguity still speculates (binder triage unchanged). Agnostic (walks FIRST sets + the position table, names NO token) + config-driven (FIRST + the rule's `lookahead`); independent review-folded — nullable-stop soundness guard + contextual-keyword precondition → `D-PARSE-PREDICTIVE-PRUNE-CONTEXTUAL-KEYWORD` + synthetic RED-on-disable tests (`ParserSpeculation.{DeepNestCastVsParenIsLinear, PrunesFirstBranchAtOffsetOneAndDirectDescends, NullableStopElementDoesNotOverPrune}`); 333 ctest. A RESIDUAL mild wall-clock super-linearity in the deep parse itself was CHARACTERIZED 2026-06-22 and promoted to its own row `D-PARSE-DEEP-NEST-RECURSION-MEMORY` — a controlled flat-chain-vs-nested experiment PROVED the parse WORK is O(N) (the "TreeBuilder/arena bookkeeping" guess first sketched here is REFUTED: a flat `0+0+…+0` chain of equal node count parses with FLAT per-element cost), so the residual [measured ~exp 1.7, not the ~exp 1.2 first estimated] is a constant-factor cost of the N-deep HOST recursion (inferred BY ELIMINATION to be memory-hierarchy behavior — not directly cache-instrumented), bounded/moot under the 256 depth cap — LOW-priority / trigger-gated. — Original characterization (audit trail):** The c-subset `operand` rule is `speculative:true` (compoundLiteral/cast/paren cast-vs-paren disambiguation; lookahead 64 = 1024-token probe budget). Deeply-nested input parses SUPER-LINEARLY (O(N²)+) in depth — measured @ cap=16: depth 20 ~0s, 100 ~3s, 300 TIMES OUT (>40s) — so deep input HANGS before the depth guard can fail loud, even at a LOW cap (the speculation descends the deep tail at the early levels, before the guard depth is reached). INDEPENDENT of the cap (repro @ 16/64/256) and of the guard (a non-speculative `kParenSchema` parses 1000 parens in ~10ms). FIX ATTEMPT 1 FAILED 2026-06-20: a code-trace MIS-diagnosed the cost as O(depth) `SpeculationProbe` state-snapshots (walker `cursorStack_`/`wrapFrameFlags_`, builder `open_`/`scopes_`); the O(1) size-truncation fix had ZERO timing effect AND broke the general non-append-only `SchemaWalker::snapshot/restore` API (`core/test_schema_walker`) — REVERTED. **MEASURED root cause 2026-06-20 (instrumented counters, NOT a code-trace):** the O(N²) is PANIC-MODE RECOVERY running INSIDE doomed speculative `castExpr` probes — `panicInSpec == panicRecovers` (100% of panics are in-probe) and `panicScanTokens ≈ tokensAdvanced` (the parser advances tokens almost solely to panic-scan inside failing cast probes, then rolls them back). For `((((0))))` the `castExpr` probe (tried BEFORE `parenExpr` in the `operand` alt) fails at each inner `(` (castTypeRef can't start with `(`) and `panicRecover` scans forward to the end-of-expression sync point = O(min(N,64)) tokens × N levels. **FIX ATTEMPT 2 FAILED 2026-06-20:** suppressing the panic-scan inside probes (`panicRecover` early-return when `speculationDepth > 0`) was correctness-safe (ctest 333-green) but COUNTERPRODUCTIVE — deep input HUNG WORSE (n=100: ~3 s → timeout, NO diagnostic emitted): the panic-scan is LOAD-BEARING for the failing probe to TERMINATE / make forward progress, NOT pure waste. REVERTED. **Correct direction (UNTRIED — a real engine rework, not a one-liner):** a CHEAP fail-fast for the cast-probe mismatch that PRESERVES termination — either (a) dispatch-level: fail the probe immediately on a required-alt no-candidate while `speculationDepth > 0` (instead of routing through panic recovery), or (b) a k-token candidate prune at the `operand` AltChoice (don't ENTER the cast/compound-literal probe when the token after `(` cannot start `castTypeBase`); both must stay agnostic (FIRST-set / generic dispatch, no language identity) and must not break cast / compound-literal / sizeof / the binder-sketch commit triage. Only manifests on deeply-nested input (valid C nests ≤4 in the corpus). | (closed — LL(k) predictive prune, direction (b)) | `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD`; `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`; `D-PARSE-PREDICTIVE-PRUNE-CONTEXTUAL-KEYWORD`; `c-subset.lang.json` operand rule |
| `D-PARSE-PREDICTIVE-PRUNE-CONTEXTUAL-KEYWORD` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out cycle 13, branch p14).** Closing the end-to-end "a contextual keyword in a speculative candidate's fixed prefix parses correctly" needed BOTH a PRUNE half (the registry's prescribed fix) AND a deeper PROBE half (the build DISCOVERED it; the anchor did not scope it → §B-surfaced, user chose build-deep). **(1) PRUNE:** a loader-derived token-id-keyed `contextualKinds` set (`computeContextualKinds` in `grammar_schema_json.cpp`, from the per-`LexemeMeaning.contextual` flags) + an O(1) `GrammarSchema::isContextualKind(SchemaTokenId)` query; `predictivePrefixPrunes` (`parser.cpp`) now `continue`s at any offset whose OBSERVED token is contextual → the candidate survives the prune. **(2) PROBE (the crux the build exposed):** even surviving the prune, the candidate's speculative probe `recoverAt(P_UnexpectedToken)`'d — the TokenLeaf MATCH GATE in `stepOnce` tests the UN-demoted keyword kind (`effectiveKind` by design does not model demotion), so the token never reached the builder's `pushToken` contextual-demotion. FIX: the match gate now MIRRORS the builder's demotion (a contextual `tokKind` ∉ expected → treat as a match when `identifierKind` IS expected) and advances the PARSER's walker with the demoted `identifierKind`, keeping it in lockstep with the builder's walker (no spurious desync-latch trip → the probe commits). Both halves AGNOSTIC (config-derived `isContextualKind`; the demotion target REUSES the parser's EXISTING `identifierKind` — the schema's resolved `Identifier` token kind, IDENTICAL to the builder's demotion this mirrors → walker lockstep) — EMPTY `contextualKinds` for a non-contextual grammar ⇒ ZERO behavior change, the deep-nest O(N) prune win preserved. (Review-noted pre-existing residual `D-PARSE-IDENTIFIER-KIND-HARDCODED-VS-CONFIG`: the parser+builder resolve the demotion target via the literal name `"Identifier"` rather than the live `semantics.identifierToken`; latent — all shipped grammars declare `identifierToken: "Identifier"` so they coincide; trigger-gated, NOT introduced here.) 374 ctest green, ZERO regression incl. **tsql** (the `reservedWordPolicy: contextual` grammar where the gate CAN fire). Pinned RED-on-disable with BOTH halves toggled INDEPENDENTLY (prune-skip off → caseId pruned; match-gate off → caseId survives prune but probe rejected → replays wrong candidate) by the synthetic contextual-keyword speculative-alt schema in `test_parser_speculation.cpp`: `ParserSpeculation.{ContextualKeywordInSpeculativePrefixNotMispruned` (soft keyword `kw` in caseId's `[A,Identifier,;]` prefix demotes + commits + asserts the `P_ContextualKeywordResolution` demotion diagnostic fired)`, HardKeywordInSpeculativePrefixStillPruned` (negative control — a HARD keyword stays pruned; the fix doesn't over-broaden)`}`. RESIDUAL: none for this anchor. — *Original OPEN characterization (audit trail):* **registered 2026-06-20 (FC13 predictive-prune soundness fold).** The LL(k) speculative-alt PREDICTIVE PRUNE (`Parser::predictivePrefixPrunes`, the O(N) deep-nest lever that landed alongside `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC`) compares a candidate's exact per-offset FIRST_k prefix against the observed token's `effectiveKind`. `effectiveKind` DELIBERATELY does NOT model contextual-keyword demotion (`parser.cpp` ~L63 — a soft keyword keeps its KEYWORD kind here; demotion to Identifier happens later in the builder against the live cursor expectedSet + scope stack). So for a grammar with contextual keywords (`contextual: true` per entry, or grammar-wide `reservedWordPolicy: "contextual"` — e.g. tsql), at an offset whose admissible set holds the demotion target (Identifier) the prune could see the keyword kind, find it absent, and WRONGLY drop a candidate the demoted token would in fact match — a silent mis-parse. NOT live today: c-subset's speculative prefixes are all hard keywords / punctuation, and tsql's lone `nameOrCall` speculative alt discriminates at offset 1 on `(` / qualified-name punctuation, not on a soft-keyword Identifier slot — so no shipped speculative candidate puts a contextual keyword in its FIXED prefix. The precondition ("sound only for grammars with no contextual / scope-resolvable kind in a speculative candidate's fixed prefix") is DOCUMENTED prominently at both `Parser::predictivePrefixPrunes` and `computePredictivePrefixes`. A clean conservative fix is deferred because no token-id-keyed "is this kind contextual" query exists today — the `contextual` flag is per-`LexemeMeaning` (lexeme-string-keyed); only the grammar-wide `reservedWordPolicy()` lever is exposed, which would NOT cover a per-keyword `contextual: true` under a Strict policy. | Add an agnostic token-id-keyed "is this SchemaTokenId a contextual/scope-resolvable kind" query (derive a `contextualKinds` set in the loader from the `contextual` LexemeMeaning flags + `reservedWordPolicy`), then make `predictivePrefixPrunes` CONSERVATIVE — skip the prune at any offset whose OBSERVED token has a contextual/scope-resolvable kind (do not constrain that offset). Must stay agnostic (no token/language naming) and preserve the deep-nest O(N) win for non-contextual grammars. Pin with a synthetic contextual-keyword speculative-alt schema whose candidate prefix admits Identifier at offset ≥1 + a soft-keyword input (RED-on-disable: the un-skipped prune drops the valid candidate). Priority: **normal (trigger-gated — first contextual-keyword speculative-alt consumer with a soft keyword in a candidate's fixed prefix).** | `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` (the prune this guards); `parser.cpp` `effectiveKind` / `peekSignificantKind`; `grammar_schema.hpp` `reservedWordPolicy` / `LexemeMeaning::contextual`; tsql `nameOrCall` |
| `D-PARSE-IDENTIFIER-KIND-HARDCODED-VS-CONFIG` | **OPEN (trigger-gated) — registered 2026-06-23 (cycle-13 pr-review LOW).** The parser (`parser.cpp:247` `identifierKind(schema->schemaTokens().find("Identifier"))`) and the tree-builder (`tree_builder.cpp` `identifierKind_`) resolve the identifier / contextual-demotion target via the LITERAL token name `"Identifier"`, NOT the live `semantics.identifierToken` config field — which the SEMANTIC + HIR layers DO read (`semantic_analyzer.cpp` `cfg.identifierToken`, `cst_to_hir.cpp` `sem.identifierToken`, 20+ sites). LATENT: all three shipped grammars (toy / c-subset / tsql) declare `"identifierToken": "Identifier"`, so the hardcoded string and the configured kind COINCIDE — no test diverges. A grammar that named its `identifierToken` something ELSE would split: name-resolution / HIR key on the configured kind while the parser/builder demotion keys on a non-existent `"Identifier"` token (invalid ⇒ contextual demotion silently no-ops, identifier-leaf handling mis-keys). Acknowledged: NOT a crash fix (already mitigated by the 64 MiB worker), NO production consumer — a robustness goal. Cap is RAISED not removed (`P_ExpressionTooDeep` backstop kept). — *Original characterization (audit trail):* **OPEN (trigger-gated) — registered 2026-06-22 (residual deep-expr parse super-linearity characterization cycle).** A deeply-nested expression like `((((0))))` parses with a residual MILD WALL-CLOCK super-linearity (measured ~exp 1.7, Debug, cap=4000 on a large-stack thread: depth 250 ≈23 ms → 500 ≈71 ms → 1000 ≈240 ms → 2000 ≈873 ms → 3000 ≈1897 ms; ns/level rises 93k→632k). DISTINCT from `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` (the now-FIXED O(N²) cast-vs-paren panic-scan blowup — that made n=300 take 154 s; GONE, n=3000 is now 1.9 s); it is the SAME residual a sibling session flagged (matching ~exp-1.7). **ROOT CAUSE — decisively localized by a CONTROLLED experiment, not a code-trace:** deep `((((0))))` (host-recursion depth = N) vs a flat `0+0+…+0` left-assoc chain (recursion depth ~2, SAME O(N) node/token count, built ITERATIVELY by the Pratt climb). The FLAT chain is perfectly O(N) — ns/level FLAT at ~20.5 µs across 250→3000, node count exactly linear — while only the NESTED case grows. Both exercise the IDENTICAL shared machinery (TreeBuilder frame open/close, the node-arena `std::vector` GEOMETRIC growth, schema-walker advance), so the "TreeBuilder/arena bookkeeping" hypothesis from the QUADRATIC row is **REFUTED**. Exhaustive code reading confirms every per-level op on the direct-descent paren path is O(1) (operand AltChoice dispatch, `candidateBranches` over the fixed 6-branch set, the LL(k) `predictivePrefixPrunes` over the fixed prefix, `peekSignificantKind`, frame open/close, ALL `SchemaWalker` ops, `finish()` once) and the lone-survivor `parenExpr` DIRECT-DESCENDS with NO `SpeculationProbe`/checkpoint/snapshot (so the O(N²)-snapshot path is not taken). The residual is therefore NOT algorithmic (PROVEN: the flat control isolates the shared WORK as O(N)) — it is a constant-factor cost of the N-deep HOST recursion, attributed BY ELIMINATION (not directly cache-instrumented) to that recursion's memory-hierarchy behavior: the live C++ call stack ≈ N × {parseExpressionAt, parsePrimary, parseUntilFrameDepth, stepOnce, walkExpression} frames PLUS the strided unwind re-access of the depth-indexed `frames`/`frameRules`/`cursorStack`/`pendingChildren` vectors as the working set outgrows cache (the rising-not-constant local exponent ~1.6→1.9 is consistent with cache-tier transitions, not a clean algorithmic O(N²)). **BOUNDED / MOOT:** `ParserConfig::maxExpressionDepth` caps depth at 256 (`D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD`; valid C nests ≤4 in the whole corpus; >256 FAILS LOUD via `P_ExpressionTooDeep`, never parses) AND the whole downstream frontend (semantic/HIR/MIR) is itself recursion-bound to the same 256 cap (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`) — so the residual only appears in a synthetic cap-raised micro-benchmark, never in production. Pinned by `ParserSpeculation.FlatChainParseWorkIsLinear` (the O(N)-WORK regression guard) + the existing `DeepNestCastVsParenIsLinear` (the deep-path O(N²)-regression guard, whose generous 8× bound is explained by this residual). | Convert the recursive-descent EXPRESSION parser (`parseExpressionAt`/`parsePrimary`/`parseUntilFrameDepth` + the `walkExpression` re-entry) to an explicit heap worklist/stack so deep nesting carries no host-recursion memory cost — AND, for any END-TO-END benefit, do the same for the recursion-bound downstream passes (`D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK`'s semantic/HIR/MIR), since the 256 cap is set by THEM. Stay agnostic (no token/rule/language identity). Pin with a deep-nest wall-clock ratio the iterative form keeps ~linear. Priority: **normal (trigger-gated — fires only if a real consumer needs expressions nested beyond the 256 cap AND the cap is first lifted by an iterative frontend; NO in-cap benefit otherwise).** | `D-PARSE-SPECULATION-OPERAND-QUADRATIC` (the O(N²) sibling this is the residual OF); `D-PARSE-DEEP-FRONTEND-STACK` (the downstream recursion bound that sets the 256 cap); `D-PARSE-EXPR-DEPTH-GUARD` (the cap); `parser.cpp` `parseExpressionAt`; tests `FlatChainParseWorkIsLinear` + `DeepNestCastVsParenIsLinear` |

| `D-FC12B-WIN64-VARIADIC-CALLEE` | ✅ **SHIPPED 2026-06-19 (FC12b).** **§B (user 2026-06-19): Option A — a closed `VaListStrategy` enum with the va_list TYPE DERIVED from the strategy, chosen over Option D (an explicit per-CC `vaListType` config field); derived avoids an unused-flexibility knob that must be kept consistent with the strategy. (Rejected extremes: a va_arg recipe-DSL, and a unified ptr-to-opaque-blob va_list — both break the bar.)** Microsoft x64 (ms_x64) variadic CALLEE support — `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_end` for SCALAR + FP types, config-driven + source/target/linker-AGNOSTIC. The per-CC va_list TYPE + lowering STRATEGY is a NEW closed enum `VaListStrategy` (`aggregate_layout.hpp`, beside `AggregateClassKind`/`BitFieldStrategy` so the SEMANTIC va_list-type injection reads it without pulling the link/target substrate): `SysVRegisterSave` (FC12a, unchanged-but-now-strategy-tagged), `HomogeneousPointer` (Win64, this cycle), `Aapcs64DualCursor` (declared, fail-loud-until-FC12c). `VaListLayout` gains `strategy` (first field) + `namedArgSlotBytes`; `x86_64.target.json` ms_x64 declares `{"strategy":"homogeneous_pointer","namedArgSlotBytes":8}`. **BLOCKER-2 (va_list TYPE per ABI):** `analyze()` gains an `optional<VaListStrategy>` param threaded from the resolved CC (pipeline reads it where it reads `aggregateLayout`); the sema injection switches on it — SysV → `__va_list_tag[1]` (24B), Win64 → `char*` (8B), AAPCS64 → loud `S_VariadicCalleeUnsupported`. A wrong sizeof(va_list) would mis-size the `ap` local + corrupt the stack — pinned `sizeof(va_list)`==8 ms_x64 / 24 sysv. **BLOCKER-1 (no-shadow contiguous base):** Win64's named-arg HOME space (rcx/rdx/r8/r9 slots = the caller's shadow space) and the 5th+ stack args are CONTIGUOUS from `totalFrameSize + callPushBytes` (NO shadowSpaceBytes — adding it would skip the home and read past every named arg). A NEW MIR leaf `VaHomeArgAreaAddr` (payload = the slot-aligned named-arg count) + LIR `va_home_arg_area` op materializes to `lea [sp + totalFrameSize + callPushBytes + payload*outgoingSlotSize]`; the Win64 prologue spills the named int regs into the SAME base (spill-target == va_arg-read-target). HIR→MIR lowers va_start (Win64) to `Store(VaHomeArgAreaAddr, ap)`, va_arg to a LINEAR pointer bump (NO diamond: Load ap → Load T → Gep +namedArgSlotBytes → Store ap), va_end to nothing. **FP-dup (PART 5):** Win64 passes each FP vararg in BOTH the xmm AND the matching integer (home) reg; the callee reads va_arg(double) from the home GPR slot, so the CALLER duplicates each register-resident FP VARARG (operand past `fixedOperandCount`) into argGprs[slot] via a NEW dedicated opcode `movq_xmm_to_gpr` (`66 REX.W 0F 7E /r`; byte-pin `movq rdx, xmm1` = `66 48 0F 7E CA`). A dedicated opcode (not `movq_xclass`) because the encoding-variant guard keys only on (operandKinds, width) and cannot disambiguate the two MOVQ directions, and `movq_xclass` is consumed bidirectionally by Bitcast — overloading would force a silent miscompile on GPR→FPR Bitcast. Every va seam dispatches on `VaListStrategy` with a fail-loud default (no half-migrated site silently runs the SysV path on a Win64 layout). Run-witnessed on PE x86_64 (this Windows host): `examples/c-subset/varargs_win64_sum` (int+double varargs, anti-folded via a mutable-global seed). | `D-FC12C-AAPCS64-VARIADIC-CALLEE` | ✅ **SHIPPED 2026-06-19 (FC12c).** AAPCS64 (ARM64-ELF) variadic CALLEE support — `va_start`/`va_arg`/`va_end` for SCALAR int+fp, config-driven + source/target/linker-AGNOSTIC, the THIRD `VaListStrategy` (`Aapcs64DualCursor`, beside SysVRegisterSave + HomogeneousPointer). `va_list = __va_list`, a typedef to the 5-field STRUCT DIRECTLY (NOT an array like SysV, NOT a pointer like Win64): `{void* __stack; void* __gr_top; void* __vr_top; int __gr_offs; int __vr_offs;}` (32B; sizeof pinned). Config = a `vaListLayout` block on `aapcs64` with the 5 field locators + GR/VR save geometry (gpSaveCount8/gpSlotBytes8/fpSaveCount8/fpSlotBytes16, regSaveAreaBytes()=192); the semantic injection + isVaList accept the struct shape for the strategy. **BLOCKER-1:** a NEW `fstur_q` opcode (STUR Qt,[Xn,#simm9], 128-bit, fixedWord `0x3C800000` — NOT `0x3C000000`=STURB which would spill 1 byte/FP slot → va_arg(double) garbage; byte-pin STUR Q0,[X1,#0]=`0x3C800020` + a disasm Imm9/MemBaseNoScale round-trip arm). The AAPCS64 prologue spills x0..x7 (GR block, 8B via the class GPR store) then v0..v7 (VR block, 16B via `fstur_q`) into the callee-local register-save-area at `vaRegSaveAreaOffset()`, ascending order. va_start inits the 5 fields: __gr_top=rsa+64, __vr_top=rsa+192, __stack=overflow base, __gr_offs=-(8-fixedGpr)*8, __vr_offs=-(8-fixedFpr)*16 (NEGATIVE i32 cursors). **BLOCKER-2:** va_arg's per-class diamond — Load the NEGATIVE class cursor, `ICmpSlt(offs,0)` (a reg slot remains while <0), reg arm: **SIGN-EXTEND the i32 cursor to i64 (SExt) BEFORE the byte Gep** (a 32-bit -40 zero-extended → 0xFFFFFFD8 ≈ +4 GiB wild addr → segfault), addr = `<gr|vr>_top + SExt(offs)`, bump by the slot stride; stack arm: addr = __stack, bump by gpSlotBytes=8 (the NSAA round-up quantum, even for a double); Phi the two → Load T. va_end = no-op. Every va seam dispatches on `VaListStrategy` with a fail-loud default. The callee reg-save-area zone is gated on strategy ∈ {SysVRegisterSave, Aapcs64DualCursor}. FIX: add `cc.indirectResultRegister`'s ordinal to the scratch avoid-set (→ x9, genuinely free). Structural pin `Aapcs64VariadicStructReturnPrologueScratchAvoidsX8` (red-on-disable verified: revert → scratch=x8) + the `_sret` qemu witness (red-on-disable: scratch=x8 → exit 0, not 126). **Also fixed a latent SHARED-regalloc bug surfaced by the FP-overflow witness:** `pickScratchRegs` (`lir_rewrite.cpp`) keyed its register-in-use mask by the GLOBAL register-table ordinal in a uint64 bitmask, but arm64's 33 GPR table slots push d31 to global ordinal 64 — past the mask → a fail-loud `out of 64-bit bound` on any function spilling an FPR up to d31 (the 9-double case). Re-keyed to an unbounded per-class `unordered_set` of global ordinals, mirroring `buildFreeLists` (lir_regalloc.cpp). Pin `LirRewrite.Arm64HighFprSpillScratchPoolHandlesOrdinalsBeyond64`. | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-16MIB` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out c12, branch feature/0-0-2-p14, 374 ctest + corpus `large_frame_beyond_16mib` exit 42 qemu-aarch64 baseline+release).** AS-BUILT (§B Option A — encoder macro, x16 baked): a NEW `EncodingSlotKind::Imm32MovzMovk` (value-bearing fixed32 slot; the encoder splits a 32-bit value lo16→word0 / hi16→word1 into the MOVZ/MOVK imm16 windows, mirroring `materializeViaMovkLadder`'s chunk split) + a NEW 3-word `fixedWords` variant per `add`/`sub`/`lea` in `arm64.target.json`, magnitude-routed by the variant `immMin:16777216`/`immMax:2147483647` guard. The macro is `MOVZ Xs,#(V & 0xFFFF)` + `MOVK Xs,#((V>>16) & 0xFFFF),LSL #16` + an EXTENDED-register op: for the sp-adjust `sub sp,sp,x16` (0xCB3063FF) / `add sp,sp,x16` (0x8B3063FF) with **x16 (AAPCS64 IP0 scratch) BAKED** into all 3 base words (NO resultSlot — sp=31 baked into the op word, validate's rule-G `imm32.movzmovk` baked-dest exemption); for the lea `add Xd,sp,Xd` (0x8B2063E0 base) SCRATCH-FREE — the displacement materializes into the lea's OWN dest reg Xd, threaded through all 3 words via resultSlot+extraResultSlots (the operand-0→rn wire sets Rn from the ACTUAL frame-base operand — sp here, so Rn=31=sp, byte-pinned; the override is general so a non-sp base would get its own Rn). The EXTENDED-register form (bit 21, option=011 UXTX) is the make-or-break: the shifted-register form (0xCB000000) would write XZR not sp → corrupt frame. AGNOSTIC (x86_64 has no imm16/movzmovk slot → never reached; slot-kind `==` + value-magnitude arithmetic only; the x16 identity is config-baked like XZR=31/sp=31). Byte-pinned (sub sp #0x1234000 → MOVZ/MOVK + 0xCB3063FF full 32-bit word; lea → MOVZ/MOVK + 0x8B2263E2; boundary pins 0xFFFFFF→2-word / 0x1000000→3-word / 0x7FFFFFFF→3-word / 0x80000000→fail-loud) + a callconv F4 structural pin (prologue's first word = `MOVZ x16` + x16 not value-allocated, durable scratch-safety) + **objdump-confirmed + run-witnessed `examples/c-subset/large_frame_beyond_16mib` exit 42 under qemu-aarch64 (baseline+release, Inlining ON) + x86_64-linux** (RED-ON-DISABLE: removing the variant's reachable range → A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant on the sub/add sp-adjust → the arm64 leg cannot produce a binary). Genuinely-unencodable residual → `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-2GIB` (row below; a >2 GiB frame goes negative through the int32 frame size → no variant matches → fail-loud). _Original deferral below._ NEW RESIDUAL of `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (FC12-deferral 2, 2026-06-22): the SCRATCH-FREE shifted-imm12 word-pair (`EncodingSlotKind::Imm12HiLo24` + the `add`/`sub`/`lea` 2-word variants `op Xd,Xn,#lo` then `op Xd,Xd,#hi,LSL #12` in `arm64.target.json`, magnitude-routed by the variant `immMin`/`immMax` guard) now lands an `add`/`sub`/`lea` IMMEDIATE in (4095, 0xFFFFFF] — a 16 MiB frame reach, covering every realistic frame (e.g. `int big[9000]` = 36000B prologue + `&big[8999]` lea). A value > 0xFFFFFF (16 MiB) STILL fails loud: the add/sub/lea variant selector rejects it (`A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant`, since `immMax:16777215` excludes it), and the encoder's `writeHiLo24` 24-bit gate (`A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange`) is the defense-in-depth backstop. No shipped corpus has a > 16 MiB single frame; this row keeps the ledger honest about the genuinely-unencodable tail. Priority: **low** (only a single function with > 16 MiB of locals). | Add a THIRD word to the macro (`#hi2,LSL #24` reaching 36 bits) OR materialize the offset into a scratch register via MOVZ/MOVK + a register-form `add/sub Xd,Xn,Xm` and select it when the value exceeds 0xFFFFFF. | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12`; `D-ASM-AARCH64-LARGE-FRAME-IMM12`; plan 13 (asm encoding) |
| `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-SCALED-IMM12` | **OPEN (trigger-gated) — registered 2026-06-24 (scaled-imm12 frame load/store close-out, branch feature/0-0-2-p14).** NEW narrower residual of `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (row above): now that the ENCODABLE scaled unsigned-offset frame load/store (`load_u`/`store_u`, LDR/STR `[Xn,#imm12]`, reach 0..4095×accessSize = 0..32760 for an 8-byte slot) is selected at the `selectFrameMemOp` chokepoint, a frame `ldr/str [sp, #off]` whose `off` is GENUINELY UNENCODABLE by BOTH the unscaled imm9 (−256..255) AND the scaled unsigned imm12 STAYS fail-loud `A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange` at the fixed32 encoder (`src/asm/format/fixed32.cpp` Imm12Scaled handler). Three sub-cases: (a) a NEGATIVE offset outside imm9 (the scaled form has no sign bit), (b) an aligned offset > 32760 (scaled field > 4095), (c) a non-access-size-aligned offset outside imm9 (the scaled field is byteOffset/accessSize — an unaligned LDR is architecturally undefined). The chokepoint keeps `baseOp` (the unscaled form) in each case → the encoder fail-louds. NOT reachable by any shipped corpus: case (a) needs a base-relative negative beyond −256 (frame offsets are non-negative sp-relative), (b) needs a single frame spill/saved-reg/stack-arg offset > 32760 B (a ~32 KB spill area — far past the deepest corpus pressure), (c) needs an unaligned frame slot (all slots are slotSize-aligned). This row keeps the ledger honest about the genuinely-unencodable tail. Priority: **low** (the closing form is the register-OFFSET LDR/STR `ldr Xt,[Xn,Xm]` or an address-materialization into a scratch — only needed for a >32 KB single-access offset or a future unaligned/negative frame access, neither of which a producer emits today). | Emit the register-offset frame form (`ldr/str Xt,[sp,Xm]` after MOVZ/MOVK-materializing the offset into a scratch `Xm`), OR materialize the address `add Xd,sp,#off` (via the shipped shifted-imm12 / MOVZ-MOVK macro) then `ldr/str [Xd,#0]` — selected when the offset fits NEITHER imm9 nor the scaled imm12; stay agnostic (slot-kind `==` + value-magnitude arithmetic, no arch/cc identity). Pin with a synthetic >32760 frame-offset case (fail-loud red-on-disable) + a runtime corpus only if a producer ever emits a >32 KB single-access frame offset. | `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (the parent, load/store-displacement half closed 2026-06-24); `D-ASM-AARCH64-LARGE-FRAME-IMM12` (the scaled-imm12 encoder + opcodes); `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-16MIB` (the add/sub/lea-immediate sibling); plan 13 (asm encoding) |
| `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-2GIB` | NEW RESIDUAL of `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-16MIB` (FC-deferral close-out c12, 2026-06-23): the MOVZ/MOVK + EXTENDED-register 3-word form (`EncodingSlotKind::Imm32MovzMovk` + the `add`/`sub`/`lea` 3-word variants in `arm64.target.json`, magnitude-routed by `immMin:16777216`/`immMax:2147483647`) now lands an `add`/`sub`/`lea` IMMEDIATE in (0xFFFFFF, 0x7FFFFFFF] — a ~2 GiB frame reach, far past any realistic frame. A value > 0x7FFFFFFF (2 GiB) STILL fails loud: the frame size flows through `emitSpAdjust`'s `static_cast<int32_t>(bytes)` and `variantImmMagnitude`'s `immInt32` (int32) — a >2 GiB magnitude goes NEGATIVE, so `variantImmMagnitude` returns nullopt → NO variant matches → `A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant`; the encoder's `writeMovzMovk` 0..0x7FFFFFFF gate (`A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange`) is the defense-in-depth backstop. No shipped corpus has a > 2 GiB single stack frame (it would itself exceed most process stack limits); this row keeps the ledger honest about the genuinely-unencodable tail. | `D-WIN64-LARGE-FRAME-STACK-PROBE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-23 (FC-deferral close-out c11, branch p14, 372 ctest + corpus `large_frame_win64` exit 42 native Windows baseline+release).** AS-BUILT: an INLINE page-walking stack probe emitted by the x86_64 encoder from a NEW `stack_probe` LIR op (chosen over `__chkstk` because dss PE exes are FREESTANDING — import only kernel32, not msvcrt where __chkstk lives; verified). Config-driven `stackProbePageBytes` on TargetCallingConvention (ms_x64=4096, all others 0/absent → no probe; validate() requires a power of two). `emitPrologue` (threaded `cc`) emits `StackProbe(sp, frameBytes, pageBytes)` when `cc.stackProbePageBytes>0 && totalFrameSize>pageBytes`, else the plain `sub rsp,F` (byte-identical small-frame/non-Windows path). The encoder hand-emits the loop `mov r11d,frame / .L: sub rsp,page / or qword[rsp],0 / sub r11d,page / cmp r11d,page / ja .L (0x77, compile-time rel8, no reloc) / sub rsp,r11` — r11 is ms_x64 caller-saved, not arg/return, probe runs before arg-home. AGNOSTIC (no `if arch/format==`; page step from the op operand, not hardcoded; arm64 OMITS the op → A_NoEncodingDeclared if ever emitted). RED-ON-DISABLE (the strongest kind): the corpus CRASHES (SIGSEGV exit 139) without the probe, exit 42 with — native on the Windows box. Byte-pins (frame 36000 non-multiple + 8192 exact-page, exact 0x77 ja) + prologue structural pins (ms_x64>4096→probe; ≤4096 + sysv>4096→plain). **★ the unforgeable native witness caught a real bug in the build: a first `sub rsp,r11` mis-encoded as `49 29 DB` (=`sub r11,rbx`) segfaulted EVEN WITH the probe → fixed to `4C 29 DC`, byte-pinned.** ORIGINALLY: **OPEN — a SILENT RUNTIME CRASH** (surfaced 2026-06-22 while adding the `large_frame_arm64` corpus, but ENTIRELY ORTHOGONAL to the arm64 fix — a pre-existing x86_64-Windows gap). DSS did NOT emit a stack-probe (`__chkstk` / page-walk) for `ms_x64` / `pe64` functions whose frame exceeds one guard page (4096B). A function like `int main(){ int big[9000]; ... }` for `x86_64:pe64-x86_64-windows-exec` emits a bare prologue `sub rsp, ~36016` that jumps ~9 pages PAST the stack guard page WITHOUT touching the intermediate pages → the first deep-slot access raises `STATUS_ACCESS_VIOLATION` (0xC0000005) at runtime. The Windows x64 ABI REQUIRES a function allocating >1 page to probe each page (`__chkstk`, or an inline `sub rsp,0x1000`/`test [rsp],eax` loop) so the guard page walks down one page at a time and the kernel commits each. Empirically verified: a 400B + a 4400B frame exit 42, a 36000B frame segfaults. Linux x86_64 + AArch64-ELF do NOT need it (kernel stack-growth guard-gap absorbs the multi-page jump — which is why `large_frame_arm64` exits 42 on x86_64-linux + qemu-aarch64). This is WHY the `x86_64:pe64` target was excluded from `examples/c-subset/large_frame_arm64/expected.json` (see its `$comment`). Priority: **normal** (a real silent-crash class on >1-page Windows frames — large local buffers; converting it to FAIL-LOUD is a cheap interim). | Implement Windows large-frame stack probing in the prologue SP-adjust (`lir_callconv.cpp` emitPrologue/emitSpAdjust), gated AGNOSTICALLY on a CC/format-declared stack-probe-threshold field (mirroring `redZoneBytes`/`shadowSpaceBytes`, NOT `if(arch=="x86_64")`): when the frame exceeds the page size, emit the page-walk probe (or a `call __chkstk`) before/in place of the single `sub rsp,N`; add a runtime corpus witness (re-add the `x86_64:pe64` target to `large_frame_arm64`) + a structural pin. INTERIM (cheaper, kills the silent crash now): a fail-loud guard refusing a >1-page ms_x64 frame until probing lands. | plan 13 (asm encoding); plan 14 (linker); `D-ASM-AARCH64-FRAME-OFFSET-BEYOND-IMM12` (the arm64 sibling, closed) |
| `D-FC12B-WIN64-STRUCT-VARARG` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-20 (FC12b-struct).** Win64 (ms_x64, `VaListStrategy::HomogeneousPointer`) struct-by-value at the variadic boundary + `va_arg(ap, struct)`. **NO new MIR op / LIR kind / carrier, NO lir_callconv / aggregate_abi change** — the design REUSED proven mechanisms: the Win64 ABI passes a by-value struct in EXACTLY ONE arg slot (pow2-≤8B → `classifyAggregate(Win64BySize)` InRegisters[1 GPR piece] = the bytes BY VALUE; ByReference → copy-to-temp + push the temp POINTER → 1 operand) + `runGpr += numGp` (==1) so a subsequent vararg's slot index is right; the SysV atomic-fit/`gpSaveCount` split + `appendByValueStackArg` carrier + the AAPCS64 guard are SKIPPED for HomogeneousPointer and PRESERVED byte-unchanged for SysVRegisterSave/Aapcs64DualCursor. **Callee (`lowerVaArgAggregate` HomogeneousPointer arm):** classify via `byValueClassify(T)` — InRegisters (≤8B) → the slot IS the storage, return apVal (the slot addr), NO extra Load (mirrors the SysV overflow-arm `return ovfArea`); ByReference (>8B) → Load the pointer from `*apVal` → the caller-copy addr; both bump `ap` by `namedArgSlotBytes` (one slot, value or pointer — NOT roundUp(size,8)), LINEAR (no diamond), mirroring the scalar HomogeneousPointer va_arg. **Pins (red-on-disable verified):** the 2 fail-loud pins INVERTED to success + 2 new (`Win64VaArgStructLeq8ReturnsSlotAddr` / `Gt8DerefsPointer` — no ICmpUle/carrier, the >8B deref adds a Load; | `D-CSUBSET-LINKAGE-UNKNOWN-SPECIFIER-DIAGNOSTIC` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-04 (cycle 14).** Built as decided (agnostic specifier-identity + fail-loud ERROR). **Mechanism**: new per-decl facet `linkageSpecifierIgnoredKinds` (the prefix's STRUCTURAL token KINDS to skip — c-subset: AttributeKeyword/ParenOpen/ParenClose); loader resolves names→SchemaTokenId (unknown→C_UnknownToken, mirrors variadicMarker; non-array/non-string→C_InvalidSemantics); `linkageFrom` skips ignored-kind tokens and emits `H_UnknownLinkageSpecifier=0xF00C` on any non-ignored prefix token missing from `linkageSpecifiers` (skip-list DEFAULT = fail-loud). Behavior = Error (NOT GCC warn-and-ignore), per the original design-lock + §A.4. Priority: **high (next cycle).** — Cycle-13 review finding (silent-failure-hunter, MEDIUM): an UNRECOGNIZED specifier identifier inside `__attribute__((...))` — a typo (`((wek))`) OR a valid-C attribute c-subset doesn't model (`((noinline))`, `((packed))`) — is SILENTLY ignored by `linkageFrom` (facet miss → no effect, no diagnostic); the decl silently keeps default (Global) linkage. NOT a valid-code miscompile (static/weak are correct + proven) and GCC-compatible leniency (GCC ignores unknown attributes with a `-Wattributes` warning), but misses the project's fail-loud preference on unrecognized input. **§B DECISION (needs user input before building)**: (a) the AGNOSTIC MECHANISM — `linkageFrom`'s flat token-walk cannot distinguish an unknown SPECIFIER from structural SYNTAX (`__attribute__`, parens) without language config; the reviewer's "Identifier-directly-under-attrSpec" distinguisher is c-subset-grammar-specific (would break agnosticism if hardcoded), so a clean fix needs the language to DECLARE which prefix tokens/positions are specifier-IDENTITIES vs pure-syntax (a new facet or a per-rule marker), then the engine emits on an identity-token that misses the facet while still skipping syntax; (b) the BEHAVIOR — Error (strict) vs Warning (GCC `-Wattributes`) vs silent-ignore (current). Priority: **normal** (missing-diagnostic on unrecognized input, not a correctness bug for valid input). | Resolve the §B (mechanism + behavior) with the user, then implement the agnostic specifier-identity recognition + emit the chosen diagnostic; pin with `__attribute__((bogus))` → diagnostic. | `D-CSUBSET-STRUCT-FNPTR-BRACE-INIT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-26 (p18 Cluster G c12, LOCAL case)** — discovered p18 c10. A struct fn-ptr member resolves + member-assigns + CALLS (c10), but LOCAL BRACE-INIT (`struct Ops a = { dbl, 5 };`) FAILED LOUD at the HIR verifier: `H_VerifierFailure: ConstructAggregate child[0] type N ≠ field type M`. ★ ROOT (NOT two distinct FnSigs — both the declarator-`fnSuffix` and the function-decl path intern the SAME `FnSig` via the shared `collectParamTypes`+`normalizeSoleVoidParams` chokepoints + `CcSysV`): a function-to-pointer DECAY GAP — the field is `Ptr<FnSig>` but the bare function name `dbl` stayed an undecayed `FnSig` DESIGNATOR (`operands(fieldPtr)[0]` IS that FnSig). Member ASSIGNMENT passes via `isAssignable`'s decay arm (which emits no node — a bare fn Ref inherently lowers to its ADDRESS at MIR), but a brace-init element must carry the field's `Ptr<FnSig>` TYPE for `ConstructAggregate`'s strict child==field equality. | ✅ Fix = option (a) TIGHT: CST→HIR `coerce` gained an `FnSig → Ptr<FnSig>` decay arm (a synthetic `Cast` lowered as a representation-free MIR `Bitcast` over the function's GlobalAddr, `mapCast(FnSig,Ptr)→Bitcast`), gated on the SAME same-signature predicate `isAssignable` uses (`tk==Ptr && operands(target)[0]==child.type`) — a SIGNATURE MISMATCH stays a loud `ConstructAggregate` verifier failure (proven: field `int(*)(int)` init with `int(int,int)` → still red). WITNESS: corpus `struct_fnptr_brace_init` (two distinct fn-ptr members + scalar field + call-through → exit 42; pe-native + elf/macho/arm64 + release arm). ★ RESIDUAL (separate anchor `D-CSUBSET-GLOBAL-AGGREGATE-RELOC-MEMBER`): a FILE-SCOPE/GLOBAL aggregate whose member is a RELOCATION (a fn-ptr `{dbl}` OR a data-ptr `{&x}`) is a PRE-EXISTING limitation (NOT a fn-ptr-specific issue, NOT this cycle's regression). | p18 Cluster G c12; cited in `examples/c-subset/struct_fnptr_brace_init/` + `src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp` (`coerce` FnSig→Ptr arm) + `src/mir/lowering/hir_to_mir.cpp` (`mapCast` FnSig→Ptr Bitcast); follows on from `D-CSUBSET-STRUCT-MEMBER-DECLARATOR` (c10). |
| `D-CSUBSET-GLOBAL-AGGREGATE-RELOC-MEMBER` | **OPEN — pre-existing limitation surfaced p18 c12, 2026-06-26; fail-LOUD, normal.** A FILE-SCOPE/global aggregate (`struct`/array) whose initializer contains a RELOCATION-bearing member — a function pointer (`struct Ops g = { dbl };`, the SQLite VFS/method-table vtable shape) OR a data pointer (`struct P g = { &x };`) — fails LOUD: `H_UnsupportedLoweringForKind ... aggregate compound-literal/initializer must be lowered into a slot by ADDRESS ... | `D-CSUBSET-PER-TARGET-STRUCT-LAYOUT` | ✅ **MECHANISM DONE 2026-06-26 (p18 Cluster G c13, plan 25); ALL 6 linux POSIX headers DONE (c14a-e); the per-target `variants` axis EXTENDED to constants/typedefs/macros + macOS errno PROVEN (c15a 187a54a / c15b 73c5763); remaining 5 macOS headers OPEN (c15c).** §B decision (user, 2026-06-26): build the FULL per-target struct-layout mechanism (not linux-x86-64-only) so macOS/arm64 SQLite are reachable without reworking descriptors. THE GAP: shipped-library `structs` were single-layout, but a field-accessed struct's byte layout DIVERGES per target — glibc `struct stat` is 144B on x86-64-linux (st_nlink 64-bit, st_mode@24 after __pad0) but 128B on arm64-linux (st_mode@16, st_nlink 32-bit) and different again on macOS (even different field NAMES: st_mtimespec vs st_mtim). libc writes the REAL struct + we read fields at OUR offsets → one layout SILENTLY corrupts data on the other targets. ★ CRUX (plan-lock-verified vs the code): x86_64/arm64 target.json `AggregateLayoutParams` BYTE-IDENTICAL (Natural+16) + `computeLayout` param-driven (no arch branch) → per-target offsets come ENTIRELY from the FIELD LIST → per-target layout = per-target field-LIST SELECTION in the decoder; injection + layout engine UNCHANGED; selection at semantic time does NOT multiply the c9 once-per-format-kind build. | ✅ MECHANISM: `ShippedStruct` gains optional `variants:[{when:{arch?,format?},fields}]` (XOR flat `fields`); `analyze()` gains `optional<string_view> activeTarget`=`target.name()` (nullopt=back-compat → flat decode, variants-only not injected); decoder EAGER-decodes all variants (anti-lurking, mirrors `signatureByDataModel`), matches `when` by GENERIC string-equality (AGNOSTIC), >1 match → `F_ShippedStructVariantAmbiguous` (0x501E, **kUnsuppressableCodes**), 0 match → not injected (reference → S_UnknownType); a variants-only descriptor DECLARES a struct surface. FIRST consumer = `sys/stat.json` `struct stat` x86_64-elf 144B + arm64-elf 128B (gated elf). ✅ DONE c14a-e: the full os_unix surface authored behind the mechanism — errno (E*+errno macro), fcntl (O_/F_ + struct flock + variadic open/fcntl via the c14c variadic-externs FFI extension), sys/stat (S_ + fstat/lstat/mkdir + S_IS* + st_*time macros), unistd (~28 fns + SEEK_/access), sys/mman (PROT_/MAP_ + mmap/munmap/mremap), pthread (fns + pthread_mutex_t shipped as a flat max-size 48B opaque typedef sidestepping the per-arch size). ✅ DONE c15a/c15b: the `variants` axis EXTENDED from structs to constants/typedefs/macros (shared `matchVariantWhen`; macros are format-only — arch isn't threaded into preprocess; 3 ambiguous-fail-loud diagnostics 0x501F-0x5021 + kUnsuppressableCodes 64→67) + `errno.json` proven on macOS (the `errno` macro → `(*__error())` macho vs `(*__errno_location())` elf; the divergent E* per-format; corpus `shipped_errno_macho` runs on the macos-latest leg). Pin: per-arch sizeof/offset (gate 6 — `shipped_struct_stat_{x86,arm64}` corpus CI + `RealSysStatPerArchLayout` unit) red-on-disable. | p18 Cluster G c13; plan 25; `src/ffi/shipped_lib_descriptor.{hpp,cpp}` + `src/analysis/semantic/semantic_analyzer.{hpp,cpp}` + `src/program/compile_pipeline.cpp` + `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/sys/stat.json` + `examples/c-subset/shipped_struct_stat_{x86,arm64}` + `tests/ffi/test_shipped_lib_descriptor.cpp`; builds on FC7 struct mechanism + c8/c9 availability; macOS constants/typedef variance extends the (scalar-closed) `D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH` theme onto this axis. |

| `D-CSUBSET-DIVISION-CORPUS-MATERIALIZE-BUG` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-04** (cycle 10r BUG FIX). Root cause identified + fixed: NOT a materialize-pass bug. The cycle-10q compound encoding packed `[REX.W 0x99, REX.W 0xF7 /7]` as a single opcode's `opcode` array. The x86-variable encoder auto-emits ONE REX prefix at instruction start computed from operand high bits (e.g., 0x41 = REX.B for R14). Per x86 decode the LAST REX before the opcode wins — the embedded second literal 0x48 (REX.W only) superseded the auto-REX, losing REX.B. IDIV operand decoded as RSI (without REX.B) instead of R14 → divide-by-zero trap. Cycle 10r SPLIT the compound into separate `cqo`/`idiv_op`/`xor_rdx_zero`/`div_op` opcodes (each a single instruction with its own auto-REX). | (closed) | plan 12 ML5 (asm encoder) + ML6 (regalloc); paired with D-CSUBSET-DIVISION-OP-CODEGEN closure |

Two pr-review folds: (1) the whole-program **merge** now remaps the `MirSymbolAddrValue.symbol` embedded id through `mergedSymbolOf` (was copied verbatim → stale abs64 target in any multi-CU build → `K_SymbolUndefined`/silent-wrong-VA); (2) the DCE liveness BFS propagates through a global's symbol-address init (release-arm corpus exposed it dropping the reloc target). Host-independent pin `MachOExecWriter.SymbolAddressDataGlobalEmitsDyldRebaseStream` (red-on-disable: rebase_size→0). | `D-CSUBSET-FN-PROTOTYPE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-22 (FC-deferral close-out loop cycle 3, branch p14).** A C function PROTOTYPE (`int f(int);`) is now a function DECLARATION that MERGES with a later definition into ONE symbol — forward/mutual recursion works (the registry trigger). **As-built (plan-locked GO-WITH-FIXES, 4 MF folded; delegated build + 3 independent verification passes):** the 3-pass pre-order already pre-binds all symbols (forward CALLS already worked); the merge hooks the Pass-1 bind-collision site with a 4-CASE direction table keyed on proto-vs-def (`SymbolRecord.isProtoDeclaration` set SYNTACTICALLY at Pass 1 via a shared `hasFnSuffixOnName` — a fn-suffix on the name's direct declarator, distinguishing a proto from a fn-pointer): **proto→def** = the DEFINITION wins the binding (`injectBinding`), proto absorbed; **def→proto / proto→proto / extern→proto** = redundant decl, keep prior, absorb the new (its name binds to its OWN record so the HIR skip + compat compare both work — a deliberate, documented deviation); **def→def / extern→def** = the existing `S_RedeclaredSymbol` (two bodies / scope-out). Pass 1.5 UPGRADES a proto's kind Variable→Function (callable) instead of `S_InvalidFunctionDeclarator`. A post-Pass-1.5 sweep compares each merged pair's resolved FnSig TypeId (interner equality = STRUCTURAL: return type + params + count + cc + variadic) → NEW `S_IncompatibleRedeclaration` (0xE022) on mismatch. | `D-CSUBSET-BITFIELD-INIT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-18 (FC8 cycle 4 "bit-field aggregate init", branch p10).** Aggregate INITIALIZATION of a bit-field struct/union now PACKS per allocation unit at all three sites (replacing the cycle-2 fail-louds): (1) LOCAL `struct S s = {…};` → `lowerBitfieldAggregateInitIntoSlot` (`hir_to_mir.cpp`) zeroes every bit-field allocation unit in a PRE-PASS (before any field value is written) then RMWs each field in via the SAME `emitBitfieldInsert` the field-by-field write uses (single packing chokepoint); ordinary fields among the bit-fields lower normally. (2) GLOBAL const init → the const-fold yields raw per-field values that the static-data byte encoder `encodeAggregateValue` (`asm.cpp`) now packs into each unit (OR `((val&mask)<<bitOffset)` into the pre-zeroed buffer). (3) `lowerConstructAggregate`'s fold path is unchanged (raw values → encoder packs); a NON-foldable bit-field RVALUE literal fails loud cleanly (→ `D-CSUBSET-BITFIELD-RVALUE-RUNTIME`). **Also fixed (C 6.7.9):** a POSITIONAL initializer now SKIPS an anonymous bit-field (`lowerBraceInit` in `cst_to_hir.cpp` — `skipAnon`), so `{a,b,c}` on a struct with an interior `unsigned : 0;` lands `c` on the real field, not the anon slot (was a silent miscompile the moment init worked). **REVIEW-CAUGHT (independent review) & folded the same cycle:** the LOCAL per-unit zeroing was initially LAZY (zero a unit on first touch, interleaved with field stores in declaration order) → an ordinary field declared BEFORE a unit-sharing bit-field (`struct { char x; int a:3; }` — `x` at byte 0, `a`'s int unit at bytes [0,4)) was CLOBBERED by that bit-field's blanket unit-zero, AND diverged from the asm encoder which pre-zeroes the whole buffer once (global `gt.x`==7 but local `lt.x`==0 — the F1 silent miscompile + global/local divergence). Fixed via the TWO-PASS above (zero ALL units, then write ALL fields — order-independent; the RMW preserves the zero in bits it does not set, ordinary fields occupy disjoint bytes; dedup on `(offset,unitBytes)` covers mixed-width units sharing an offset). | `D-CSUBSET-CHAR-STRING-VALUE-CODEGEN` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-16 (char value codegen cycle, branch p8).** Full `char` VALUE codegen on BOTH targets via a sub-native BYTE width axis (`kLirInstFlagWidth8`): byte LOAD (x86 movzx r/m8 / arm64 LDURB — zero-extending, byte-exact), byte STORE (x86 mov r/m8,r8 + forceRexPrefix / arm64 STURB), byte SEXT (x86 movsx r/m8 / arm64 SXTB — char→int widening). The width-8 flag is CONFINED to {load, store, sext}: `memAccessWidthFlags(Char)=8` at every memory site (load/store/folded-rip-load+predicate/Extract/InsertValue); `registerOpWidthFlags` collapses char's byte width→32 for PLUMBING (const/copy/Trunc — no 8-bit register form; value consumed low-bits-only); char COMPUTE never occurs (integer promotion → I32) and would fail LOUD (no width-8 ALU variant). String-value rodata (`char* p="abc"; *p`) loads via the existing rodata producer + byte load. Indexed char access (`p[n]`, x86 SIB byte forms) works on x86; arm64 indexed is blocked by a PRE-EXISTING arm64 `lea` (symbol-only) gap affecting int+char alike — NOT a char limitation. Pins: 5 LIR width flags (red-on-disable demonstrated) + 2 asm byte-word pins (exact bytes, both targets) + `char_value` (cross-target, exit 132, sign-correct) + `char_ptr_indexed` (x86 indexed, exit 131). | `D-FC7-STRUCT-BY-VALUE-ARG-RETURN` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-16 (FC7 C3, branch p9, commits d25696d + 03ba02d) — ALL 4 ABIs done.** C3 = AAPCS64 + Apple arm64 via the **IRR-reroute design** (§B Option A — explicit indirect-result register, refined at build time from the plan-lock's `WriteIndirectResult` op, which was UNSOUND because x8 is allocatable: emitting `mov x8,R` before arg-setup could clobber an arg parked in x8). | `D-FC7-SYSV-STRUCT-RETURN-IN-REGS` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-16 (FC7 C1c, §B Option A, commit 1016d47).** A struct/union RETURNED by value now works across ALL SysV return classes. **§B (user) = Option A: a new MIR `ReturnPiece` opcode** (the caller-side mirror of `Arg`) for the multi-register capture — over (B) a side-table + post-regalloc memory synthesis or (C) sret-everything (ABI-non-conformant for ≤16B, rejected). **As-built:** (1) **callee** loads the eightbyte pieces and emits a MULTI-operand `Return` (maxOp bumped to N); the lir_callconv materialization moves each piece → `returnReg[class][per-class cursor]`. (3) **sret** (>16B MEMORY): a hidden result-pointer `Arg` (GPR ordinal 0, shifting the real params via the shared `ArgOrdinalCounter`) the callee copies the result through (`lowerByteWiseCopy`) + returns; no new opcode. DISCOVERED 2026-06-16 during FC7 closeout Cycle B — NOT an FC7 anchor (pre-existing, general array-indexing gap, unrelated to aggregate copy). | Indexing a STORAGE array (an array LOCAL or struct field, baseKind≠Ptr) lowers in `hir_to_mir.cpp` `lowerLvalueAddress` Index arm to a **3-op GEP `[basePtr, 0, idx]`** (the leading 0 steps through the pointer-to-array), but `mir_to_lir.cpp` `lowerGep` does NOT lower the 3-op shape → fail-loud `L_UnsupportedLoweringForOpcode` (deferred opcode) on BOTH targets. POINTER indexing (`p[i]`, 2-op `[ptr,idx]`) works; storage-array indexing never did. | `D-LIR-INT-MEMORY-WIDTH-EXACT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-17 (array-storage cluster, branch p9, user §B "all widths, one cycle").** DISCOVERED by the array work's self-audit: integer memory access was 8-byte-wide for every int except `char` (`memAccessWidthFlags` returned width-default; the x86/arm64 schemas had only width-64 + width-8 mem variants), so a 64-bit load/store of a PACKED sub-8-byte element (array element or struct field) overran — `array_storage_index` CRASHED (ACCESS_VIOLATION) under the REAL release pipeline; FC7 struct-field writes were latently affected too. | `D-CSUBSET-INDEX-INTEGER-PROMOTION` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-22 (FC-deferral close-out loop cycle 4, branch p14).** A `char` subscript of a WIDE-element array/pointer (`int a[N]; char c; a[c]`) now integer-PROMOTES to `int` (C 6.3.1.1 / 6.5.2.1) BEFORE the index arithmetic. **As-built (small, front-end, the BEST-long-term placement — not a MIR band-aid):** the CST→HIR `Index` lowering (`cst_to_hir.cpp` ~1862) coerces a sub-int index via the SAME `integerPromotedType`+`coerce` the binary-op path uses (config-driven C 6.3.1; gated on `arith_.has_value()` so block-less toy/tsql are byte-identical) — so the HIR index node is already `int` and `scaleIndexToBytes` sees a promoted index. **`builder.makeIndex` has EXACTLY ONE call site** in all of `src/` (independently verified), so EVERY subscript — rvalue load, lvalue store, compound-assign, `&a[i]`, `a[i]++` — funnels through the one promoted chokepoint (no §A.5 multi-site miss). The crux is OVERFLOW: an un-promoted `(char)100 * 4` = 400 wraps mod 256 → reads/writes the WRONG element; promotion computes 400 at int width. Signedness preserved (signed `char`→SExt, unsigned→ZExt; a negative index sign-extends). int/long index untouched (`integerPromotedType` returns the same TypeId → no coerce). **Witnesses:** corpus `index_integer_promotion` exit 42 — char load AND char-indexed STORE both overflow-sensitive (`c=100`/`d=120`, value-divergent) + signed-char — on x86_64-PE (ctest) + x86_64-ELF (WSL) + arm64-ELF (qemu) [macho macos leg]; MIR pin `CharIndexIntegerPromotesToI32BeforeStrideMul` (the stride `Mul` is I32-typed, its lhs is the SExt/ZExt promotion not the raw char Arg) DEMONSTRATED red-on-disable (promotion off → inst-count 8→7, Mul Char-typed, example walls/overflows). Independent review VERIFIED-CLEAN. 365/365 ctest. **SHORT residual (orthogonal, fail-loud, NOT this anchor):** a `short` index promotes CORRECTLY (the cycle emits the SExt) but the I16 SExt/Trunc ENCODING is unrealized at the backend → loud `L_UnsupportedLoweringForOpcode` on x86 + arm64 — the separate sub-native I16-codegen gap `D-CSUBSET-32BIT-ALU-FORMS`/`D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS`, NOT the promotion. — ORIGINAL: First need a `char`/`short`-typed subscript of a WIDE-element array/pointer (`int* a; a[c]` where `c` is `char`) to compile. DISCOVERED 2026-06-17 (array-storage cluster re-audit, NIT). Today FAIL-LOUD (NOT a miscompile — and strictly better than the pre-cycle SILENT scale-1 form): `scaleIndexToBytes` types the scaling `Mul(idx, stride)` at the index's OWN type (`hir.typeId(kids[1])`), so a `char` subscript makes a `Char`-typed Mul that walls at the Char-ALU gap (`D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS`). Per C 6.3.1.1 the subscript should integer-PROMOTE to `int` before the index arithmetic — a pre-existing FRONT-END promotion gap the scaling faithfully reflects. `char`-index-of-`char`-array (stride 1, no Mul) and `int`-index both work. | (closed) | `cst_to_hir.cpp` Index lowering (integerPromotedType+coerce); `D-CSUBSET-32BIT-ALU-FORMS`/`D-CSUBSET-SUBNATIVE-ALU-FORMS` (the orthogonal I16-codegen gap blocking the short end-to-end); `D-MIR-STORAGE-ARRAY-INDEX-GEP` (the cycle that surfaced it) |

| `D-FFI-SHIPPED-LIB-PLATFORM-SELECT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-09 — DISSOLVED by Model 3** (the `#include puts("hello")` 3-OS string-FFI capstone cycle). The per-platform-dir SELECTION problem this anchor tracked no longer exists: the 15 per-platform `shippedLibs/<os-arch>/<h>.json` descriptors were COLLAPSED into 5 **NEUTRAL** `shippedLibs/<h>.json`, each carrying platform-neutral signatures + a per-format **`library` MAP** `{pe,elf,macho}`; `shippedLibDirs` became the single neutral root `["shippedLibs"]`. The map is threaded target-AGNOSTICALLY through the front-end (descriptor→`ShippedExternSymbol`→`HirExternRecord`) and resolved to ONE library string per-target LATE, at `compile_pipeline.cpp` (via `objectFormatKindName(format.kind())`; missing key → `externLibraryByFormat` fallback; unknown key → fail loud) — so there is no longer a *directory* to pick by active target, and the front-end stays target-blind. This is **dissolution, NOT the registry's hinted per-dir platform-predicate remediation** (that fix is no longer needed — the platform axis moved INTO the neutral descriptor as the format-keyed library map). Cite: the Model-3 §B decision (plan-00 §0.2). — ORIGINAL trigger/context retained below. FF11 (2026-06-05, cycle 18+; was STILL OPEN after v0.0.2 V2-2 2026-06-06): the angle-form `#include <h>` system search path (`SemanticConfig.shippedLibDirs`) lists its platform EXPLICITLY (c-subset ships `["shippedLibs/windows-x86_64"]`, the only dir). Trigger = the FIRST time a SECOND platform's shipped-lib descriptors land (e.g. a `shippedLibs/linux-x86_64/` with a libc-flavored `stdio.json` descriptor) AND a single c-subset source must compile to BOTH — the resolver would then need to PICK the dir matching the active target (`ObjectFormatKind` / OS / arch) instead of searching every declared dir. Today: `applySystemDirs` (program.cpp) resolves EVERY `shippedLibDirs` entry and the resolver searches all of them, so a Windows + Linux shipped pair would both be on the path (first-match wins → wrong-platform descriptor could shadow). Priority: **normal** (the single-dir path is correct for the Win64-only corpus). UPDATE (2026-06-08, shippedLibs build-out): the `linux-x86_64` + `macos-arm64` descriptor sets NOW EXIST (stdio/stdlib/string/ctype/math each, all decode-validated by `AllShippedDescriptorsDecode`) — so the trigger's "a SECOND platform's descriptors land" half HAS fired. But they are STAGED data only: c-subset `shippedLibDirs` still lists ONLY `["shippedLibs/windows-x86_64"]`, so nothing is on the path to shadow and no source compiles to a non-Windows target yet. The REMAINING (unfired) trigger half is purely the resolver needing to SELECT the dir by active target. NOTE: V2-2 (2026-06-06) replaced the c-subset-source `stdio.h` with the neutral JSON descriptor (`D-FFI-SHIPPED-LIB-DESCRIPTOR-AGNOSTIC` ✅); the platform-select mechanism is unchanged. | Add a per-`shippedLibDirs`-entry platform predicate (e.g. `{ "dir": "shippedLibs/linux-x86_64", "format": "elf", "os": "linux" }`) OR derive the platform subdir from the active target spec at `applySystemDirs` time; the resolver then searches only the matching dir(s). Keep it config-driven (the language declares the platform axis; the engine selects) — NO `if (format == pe)` in the resolver. | `D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE` | A shipped-lib descriptor (`shippedLibs/<platform>/*.json`, V2-2 2026-06-06) needs a VARIADIC function (e.g. `printf`) OR a signature form the shared `parseTypeFromText` codec does not yet accept.
