| `D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — format-driven extern-call dispatch (the fix for a CONFIRMED latent x86_64-ELF FFI miscompile). The plan-lock proved byte-level that the ELF linker points an extern's `symbolVa` at its PLT STUB (code: `jmp [GOT]`), yet MIR→LIR unconditionally emitted `call_indirect_via_extern` (`FF 15` = `call [rip+disp32]`), dereferencing the stub's bytes as a function pointer → SIGSEGV. The extern-call shape is a property of the OBJECT FORMAT, not the CPU target (x86_64-PE vs x86_64-ELF need OPPOSITE opcodes). Fix: new closed enum `ExternCallDispatch` (`core/types/object_format_kind.hpp`) + a per-format `externCallDispatch` field on `ObjectFormatSchema` (`indirect-slot` = PE IAT / Mach-O __got, deref a pointer slot via `call_indirect_via_extern`; `direct-plt` = ELF, plain direct `call`/BL to the linker-synthesized PLT stub). `lowerToLir`/`lowerCall` selects the opcode from the active format's value as DATA — ZERO `if (arch/format == …)`; ELF needs NO new codegen opcode (reuses the existing `call`/BL→PLT-stub). The 4 live exec formats declare it (pe64 + macho64-x86_64 = `indirect-slot`; elf64-x86_64 + elf64-aarch64 = `direct-plt`). NOT validate-required (an exec format built for a non-FFI purpose may omit it); the real fail-loud is at LOWERING — a module with extern imports under a nullopt-dispatch format → `L_RequiredLirOpcodeMissing`; an unknown value → load fail-loud. Pins: `MirToLir.{ExternCallEmitsCallIndirectViaExternOpcode, ExternCallOnDirectPltFormatEmitsPlainCall, ExternImportsWithNoDispatchFailLoud, IndirectSlotWithoutOpcodeFailsLoud}` + the `extern_call_elf` runtime corpus (x86_64-ELF `abs` FFI → exit 42; RED-on-disable by flipping the ELF format to `indirect-slot`). | (closed) | plan 14 linker + plan 11 FFI |
| `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — the END-TO-END ARM64-ELF runnable FFI call-WITH-RESULT path is complete. **The gap was the `lea`/GlobalAddr lowering, NOT a "reg-move-class op"** (the D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH cycle's first guess) — empirically re-confirmed this cycle: with the arm64 `lea` opcode disabled, BOTH the MIR→LIR fixture AND the `extern_call_elf` arm64 compile fail with the EXACT diagnostic `L_RequiredLirOpcodeMissing: target 'arm64' declares no 'lea' opcode (required for lowering MIR GlobalAddr)` — the raw `lowerToLir` lowers a `Call`'s callee `GlobalAddr` via `lowerGlobalAddr`→`lea` (the peephole that folds the symbol into the call's SymbolRef is an OPTIMIZED-path thing, absent in the raw lowering). The D-AS4-3 ARM64 `lea` (ADRP+ADD, commit 92386d3) supplied the missing opcode; this cycle PROVES the FFI path: (1) the MIR→LIR pin `MirToLir.Arm64ExternCallWithResultLowersUnderDirectPlt` (the dropped pin, reconstructed — lowers clean, 2 direct calls, 0 indirect; RED-on-disable demonstrated above), (2) the runnable corpus `examples/c-subset/extern_call_elf` gained an `arm64:elf64-aarch64-linux-exec` arm (compiles host-independently → valid AArch64 ELF; RUNS on the native `ubuntu-24.04-arm` CI leg + qemu via the cross-arch gate → exit 42). The ELF-aarch64 PLT/GOT (`emitArm64PltStub`, D-LK6-8 ✅) + the format-driven `direct-plt` dispatch (D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH ✅) complete the chain. **⚠️ CORRECTION (2026-06-08, same-day next cycle): the "→ exit 42" RUNTIME claim above was an OVER-CLAIM** (exactly the runtime risk that cycle's own self-audit flagged). The compile-to-valid-AArch64-ELF half was real, but the binary SIGSEGV'd at runtime (CI exit 139; locally reproduced under qemu once the file's execute bit was set). Root cause = a SEPARATE codegen bug, NOT the FFI path: non-leaf ARM64 functions did not spill the link register x30, so `main`'s epilogue `ret` returned to a clobbered LR (an infinite self-loop overrunning the stack). The FFI dispatch itself was always correct — `abs(7-49)` returned 42 in x0. The corpus GENUINELY runs to exit 42 only after `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER` (below) landed the x30 spill. | (closed — runtime corrected by the NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER fix) | plan 14 (D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64 family); D-AS4-3 (the lea that closed the compile path); D-FFI-EXTERN-CALL-DISPATCH + D-LK6-8 (the PLT/dispatch chain); D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER (the x30 fix that made it actually run) |
| `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-NONLEAF-LINK-REGISTER` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — non-leaf ARM64 functions now spill + reload the link register x30. **This is the ACTUAL root cause of the arm64-FFI SIGSEGV (CI exit 139)** that `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL`'s "→ exit 42" over-claimed away (the prior cycle's self-audit had flagged exactly this runtime risk). A calling convention that carries the return address in a LINK REGISTER (AAPCS64 x30) rather than pushing it on the stack (x86_64 `call`; callPushBytes=8) makes x30 live across the whole body of a non-leaf function — every `bl`/`call` clobbers it. The frame logic spilled the `calleeSaved` set (x19–x29) but NOT x30 (deliberately the `linkRegister`, NOT in `calleeSaved`, so it stays un-allocatable), so `main`'s epilogue `ret` returned to the clobbered LR (the address after the last call) → an infinite self-loop whose repeated epilogue `add sp` walked SP off the stack into a guard page → SIGSEGV. **The FFI dispatch was always correct** — `abs(7-49)` returned 42 in x0; the PLT stub (ADRP x16/LDR x17/BR x17) + the GLOB_DAT relocation both worked. **Fix** (`src/lir/lir_callconv.cpp::materializeOneFunc`, agnostic + config-driven): when `hasCalls && cc.linkRegister.has_value()`, fold the link register into `savedRegs` so the existing prologue/epilogue machinery spills it at entry + reloads it before `ret`. ZERO `if(arch/format==…)` — x86_64 (no `linkRegister`) takes the no-op path; the schema's long-declared `linkRegister` field (whose `target_schema.hpp` comment PROMISED "ML7 lowering checks linkRegister.has_value()") is finally consumed. **Pins**: `LirCallconv.NonLeafAarch64FunctionSpillsLinkRegister` (non-leaf SAVES x30 + leaf does NOT; RED-on-disable: revert the fold → x30 absent → fail) + `LirCallconv.NonLeafX8664FunctionHasNoLinkRegisterToSpill` (agnosticism control: x86_64 cc has no linkRegister → no-op path) + the `extern_call_elf` arm64 runtime corpus (now genuinely exit 42 under qemu + native-arm64; was SIGSEGV → CI red — so red-on-disable by construction). **+ HOST-INDEPENDENT BYTE-PIN (2026-06-08, same-day hardening)**: `LirCallconv.NonLeafAarch64FramePrologueEpilogueByteExact` drives the real production tail (legalizeTwoAddress → materializeCallingConvention → assemble) and byte-pins the ASSEMBLED non-leaf prologue+epilogue EXACT — incl. `stur x30,[sp,#16]` (f80103fe) at prologue offset 12 + `ldur x30,[sp,#16]` (f84103fe) reloaded before `ret` — against hand-verified ARM-ARM literals, plus a leaf-control (g spills x28/x29 but no `stur x30`). RED-on-disable DEMONSTRATED (disable the fold → frame 0x20→0x10 → both byte windows diverge). Closes the gap where the COMPOSED frame's byte-correctness was witnessed ONLY by the native-arm64 runtime leg (the per-instruction arm64 byte-pins prove instructions in isolation, never the composed frame). The THREE layers — structural (savedRegs, every leg) + this byte-pin (assembled bytes, every leg incl. Windows MSVC) + runtime corpus (exit 42, native-arm64 leg) — are complementary; none replaces another. 207/207 (no frame-size regression — x86_64 has no linkRegister so its frames are byte-identical; no arm64 non-leaf frame-size pin existed pre-fix). | (closed) | plan 14 (D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64 family); `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL` (the over-claim this corrected); `D-LK10-ENTRY-ML7-FRAME-BIAS-UNIFY` (the frame substrate it extends); `target_schema.hpp` linkRegister field |
| `D-AS3-BLOCK-REL-IMM19/26` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — AArch64 intra-function branch displacement resolution. The cycle-13.5 substrate (`BlockRelPatchKind { X86Rel32, Arm64Imm19, Arm64Imm26 }` on `BlockRelPatch`) left the two ARM64 arms as a fail-loud stub (`A_NoEncodingShapeWalker`); this cycle implements the real resolver in `src/asm/asm.cpp`. The displacement is PC-relative TO THE INSTRUCTION ITSELF (`disp = (target - patchOffset) >> 2`, NO +4 bias — unlike x86 rel32's relative-to-after-the-disp) and SCALED by 4 (branch targets are word-aligned); Imm19 (B.cond) occupies bits 5..23, Imm26 (B) bits 0..25. The resolver READ-MODIFY-WRITES only that bit-field (a `writeU32LEAt` would clobber the opcode/cond bits), masks the two's-complement displacement to the field width BEFORE the shift (negative-disp sign bits cannot bleed past the field), asserts 4-byte alignment (`A_NoMatchingEncodingVariant` on a non-multiple delta — never a silent low-bit drop), and signed-range-checks against the field width (`A_ImmediateOperandOutOfRange`; >reach → `D-CSUBSET-LONG-BRANCH` thunk is the future generalization). The fixed32 encoder selects `Arm64Imm19`/`Arm64Imm26` purely from `wire.slotKind` (config-driven; the new `EncodingSlotKind::Imm19={5,19}` added in lockstep) and queues a `BlockRelPatch` into `blockPatches`. ZERO `if(arch/format==…)` — the dispatch is on config-selected patch-kind DATA, symmetric with the x86 `X86Rel32` arm. **Pins**: `LirCallconv.Arm64ControlFlowSkeletonEncodesCmpBcondBWithResolvedOffsets` — a 6-word byte-exact pin through the real `assemble()` path covering forward Imm19 (+2), forward Imm26 (+3), and the **negative Imm26 back-edge** (−4 → `0x17FFFFFC`, two's-complement); RED-on-disable DEMONSTRATED (remove the `>>2` scaling → `0x14000003`→`0x1400000C` + `0x17FFFFFC`→`0x17FFFFF0`). **Runtime**: the `arm64_control_flow` while-loop corpus (exit 42) executes the resolved branches end-to-end — PROVEN LOCALLY under qemu-aarch64 (exit 42 ×3); the native `ubuntu-24.04-arm` CI leg (real arm64 hardware) CONFIRMED it GREEN — run 27170873148, 2026-06-08 (§A.5 cross-target runtime closure SATISFIED). | (closed — runtime CONFIRMED green on the native ubuntu-24.04-arm CI leg, run 27170873148) | plan 13 §AS3 (block-rel substrate, cycle-13.5); plan 14 (D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-CONTROL-FLOW); `D-CSUBSET-LONG-BRANCH` (the >reach thunk, still open) |
| `D-AS3-COND-CODE-ARM64` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-08** — AArch64's condition-code table + the generic cond-placement knobs. `arm64.target.json` now declares a `condCodeEncoding` table (10 entries: eq:0 ne:1 slt:11 sle:13 sgt:12 sge:10 ult:3 ule:9 ugt:8 uge:2) consumed by BOTH `jcc` (B.cond, the cond nibble at bits 0..3) AND `setcc` (CSET). The cycle generalized `condCodeFromPayload` with two NEW template fields — `condBitPos` (uint8, default 0) + `condInvert` (bool, default false) — so the SAME generic encoder line (`words[0] |= (condNib & 0x0F) << condBitPos`) serves x86 (the defaults → byte-identical to pre-knob) AND ARM64 B.cond (condBitPos=0) AND ARM64 CSET (condBitPos=12, condInvert=true: `CSET Xd,cond` = `CSINC Xd,XZR,XZR,invert(cond)`, the AArch64 cond-inversion `cond ^ 1`). ZERO `if(arch==…)` — the bit position + inversion are config DATA. Fail-loud: a variant declaring `condCodeFromPayload` on a schema with no `condCodeEncoding` table errors. **Pins**: `Arm64Encoder.CsetEncodesInvertedCondAtBits12` (cset x0,gt=`0x9A9FD7E0` GT 0xC→0xD; cset x0,eq=`0x9A9F17E0` EQ 0x0→0x1 — two conditions defeat a "constant nibble" bug; RED-on-disable DEMONSTRATED: disable `condNib ^= 1u` → 0xD7→0xC7) + `Arm64Encoder.ZextEncodesOrrW` (zext x0,w1=`0x2A0103E0`) + the B.cond cond-at-bit-0 path pinned via the skeleton's `b.sgt`=`0x5400004C`. **Runtime**: the `arm64_control_flow` corpus exercises cmp+jcc end-to-end (PROVEN LOCALLY under qemu, exit 42; native-arm64 CI CONFIRMED green, run 27170873148). Note: lowerCondBr FUSES the loop's ICmp into cmp+B.cond, so the separately-lowered setcc(CSET)/zext are emitted-but-dead in that corpus — their CORRECTNESS is pinned host-independently by the byte-tests, not the corpus. | (closed — runtime CONFIRMED green on the native ubuntu-24.04-arm CI leg, run 27170873148) | plan 13 §AS3 (cond-code table, cycle-13.5); pairs with `D-AS3-BLOCK-REL-IMM19/26` |

| `D-OUTPUT-EXEC-BIT` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-24 (deferral loop iteration 1, branch feature/0-0-2-p16).** `writeImage` now sets the POSIX execute bits (owner/group/others, `std::filesystem::permissions(..., perm_options::add)`) on an executable-flavor output; `compile_pipeline::linkAndWrite` decides executability CONFIG-DRIVENLY via `ObjectFormatSchema::isImageFlavor()` (no arch/format identity branch — `writeImage` switches on a `bool executable = false`, staying format-blind). Discovered 2026-06-08 while root-causing the arm64-FFI failure — the 0644 mode masked the real x30 SIGSEGV under a *manual* `qemu-aarch64 <file>` invocation (ENOEXEC fired before any guest code ran). Trigger = the first non-test consumer running a `--output` binary directly, OR a decision to ship runnable-out-of-the-box output. | `D-LK1-ELF-EXEC-DATA-SECTIONS` | 🟡 **RODATA PATH CLOSED (rodata-only scope)** — the ELF ET_EXEC writer (`src/link/format/elf.cpp`) now emits a loadable `.rodata` section from `module.dataItems` (SHF_ALLOC, folded into the single R+X `.text` PT_LOAD via `shFlagsToPFlags`; data-symbol VAs added to the static `symbolVa` map so code→rodata relocations resolve through `applyExecRelocations`). So a string-literal pointer arg to a dynamic FFI call (`puts("hello")`) now lands its data in `.rodata` on the dynamic path too; runtime-proven by the `shipped_include_puts` corpus → stdout `"hello\n"` + exit 42 on linux-x86_64 (WSL) AND linux-arm64 (qemu). **WRITABLE PATH CLOSED 2026-06-19** (by `D-LK4-DATA-PRODUCER-MUTABLE-GLOBAL`): writable `.data` + zero-fill `.bss` now emit into a SEPARATE 2nd R+W PT_LOAD (W^X; bss extends p_memsz not p_filesz), on BOTH the static + dynamic ELF arms — runtime-proven (`global_write` exit 42 x86_64-ELF WSL + arm64-ELF qemu). **STILL DEFERRED:** the data→data dataItem-reloc path (`D-LK1-ELF-RODATA-DATAITEM-RELOC`). Historical context — the original blocker: the ELF ET_EXEC writer emitted only `.text`/`.symtab`/`.strtab`/`.shstrtab` — NO data section. So a module-level data global (`int g = 42;`) could not reach an ELF executable. This is the blocker for a RUNNABLE ARM64 `lea` corpus: the D-AS4-3 ARM64 `lea` (ADRP+ADD) encoder is built + proven by byte-pins (`Arm64Encoder.Lea*`) + the linker reloc-formula tests (`test_aarch64_reloc_formulas.cpp`), but an end-to-end `static int g=42; int *p=&g; return *p;` corpus that exercises lea→load→exit-42 needs `g` in a loadable data section (and a 2nd R+W PT_LOAD), which the static ET_EXEC path lacks. Same gap affects x86_64-ELF data globals (the format-dispatch cycle's `extern_call_elf` corpus avoided strings for exactly this reason). NOTE (2026-06-08): the FFI direct-call path that REQUIRES the lea to COMPILE now runs end-to-end (`extern_call_elf` arm64 arm → `D-LK10-ENTRY-ARM64-FFI-ISEL` ✅ CLOSED) — but that exercises the lea on the COMPILE path only (the lea materializes `&abs` yet the direct BL targets the symbol via the PLT, so the lea's runtime RESULT is dead there). OBSERVING the lea's runtime VALUE still needs either this data-global deref path OR an indirect call through a function POINTER (`D-ML7-2.4`, a separate isel gap). **UPDATE 2026-06-12 (FC4 c2): the fn-pointer option LANDED — `D-ML7-2.4` closed; the `fnptr_call`/`fnptr_callback` arm64-ELF arms BLR through an ADRP+ADD-materialized `&helper` at RUNTIME (qemu exit 42), so the arm64 lea's runtime VALUE is now observed end-to-end.** Priority: **normal** (the lea ENCODER, the user-directed deliverable, is complete + strongly pinned; only the lea's runtime-VALUE observation is gated). | Extend the ELF ET_EXEC writer to lay out a `.rodata`/`.data` section with the module's `AssembledData` bytes, assign each data symbol a VA, add a 2nd page-aligned PT_LOAD (R[+W]), and let the existing relocation applier patch code→data references. Then reuse `global_int`-style sources (`int g=42; return g;`) with an `arm64:elf64-aarch64-linux-exec` target arm under the qemu/native cross-arch gate → exit 42 proves lea→load end-to-end. | plan 14 LK1 (ELF exec data sections); pairs with `D-AS4-3` (the lea encoder it would make runnable) + the `D-LK4-RODATA-PRODUCER-*` family (the constant-encoding walker) |

| `D-LK1-MACHO-RODATA-DATAITEM-RELOC` | First Mach-O `__const` rodata item carrying its OWN relocation (a data→data reference — e.g. a const pointer table / 8-byte rodata pointer slot). **F5 UPDATE (2026-06-25):** `exec_data_section.hpp` now PATCHES such relocs in-place (`applyDataItemRelocations`, `allowItemRelocations=true`), but `macho.cpp` then fails loud (`K_NoMatchingObjectFormat`) on any abs64 site collected from `__TEXT,__const` — because that segment is read-execute + code-signed and dyld CANNOT PIE-rebase it (a relocated pointer is inherently load-writable). F5's own symbol-address pointers DODGE this: the asm arm forces them to `.data` (writable). So this trigger now fires only for a FUTURE const-with-relocs item the front-end places in rodata. Priority: **normal** (fail-loud today; no producer emits rodata data→data relocations). | Route reloc-bearing rodata to a WRITABLE-AT-LOAD `__DATA_CONST` segment (Apple's const-reloc idiom — writable during dyld fixup, read-only after) + emit its rebase entries (the F5 `dyldRebaseBlob` machinery, segment index `__DATA_CONST`), instead of the sealed `__TEXT,__const`. | plan 14 LK1 / LK3-RODATA (Mach-O exec data sections); shares the `exec_data_section.hpp` guard with `D-LK1-ELF-RODATA-DATAITEM-RELOC`; cited by `macho.cpp` F5 const-site guard; mirrors PE `D-LK4-RODATA-WALKER-RELOC-BASE-OFFSET` |

| `D-LK-RODATA-HELPER-PE-PARITY` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-24 (deferral loop, branch feature/0-0-2-p16) — ALREADY-SATISFIED (stale-open row), verified this cycle.** PE was retrofitted onto the shared helper by the **D-LK4-DATA-PRODUCER** cycle: `pe.cpp` calls `buildExecDataSection` (660-677) + `addDataSymbolVas` (921-938) for ALL three section kinds — NO inline rodata→symbolVa loop remains (the premise of this row is stale). **M1** (anonymous-`SymbolId{}` skip) is handled by `addDataSymbolVas` and chokepoint-tested via `test_elf_exec_writer.cpp:2107` (PE inherits it by-construction through the shared chokepoint). **H1** (over-aligned item) is **STRUCTURALLY IMPOSSIBLE** for PE, not merely masked: the `Alignment` type CAPS at 256 bytes (`alignment.hpp` `fromBytes`/`of<N>` reject > 256) while PE `sectionAlignment` is ≥ page (4096), so a section's `maxAlign` can NEVER exceed its alignment — a `checkMaxAlign` fail-loud guard would be untestable dead code (no constructible over-aligned item). | `D-LK6-AARCH64-ADDABSLO12-HIGH-VA` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-09 — RUNTIME-PROVEN on Apple Silicon** (run **27192415923**, same witness as `D-LK1-MACHO-EXEC-DATA-SECTIONS`: the `macos-clang-release` leg ran `global_int` macos-arm64 → ctest **#184 Passed** → exit 42, which means the high-VA ADD_ABS_LO12_NC reloc RESOLVED at runtime — else exit ≠ 42). Cited at `exec_reloc_apply.hpp` `Aarch64AddAbsLo12`. The ADD_ABS_LO12_NC ("No Check") reloc applier carried an ELF-centric `S+A ≤ UINT32_MAX` upper bound that WRONGLY rejected valid Mach-O PIE VAs (which sit above the 4 GiB `__PAGEZERO`, e.g. 0x1'0000'4040) — it blocked the macOS-arm64 data-global access path (`global_int` → `__const`). Root cause: `(S+A) & 0xFFF` is a magnitude-INDEPENDENT low-12 extraction (the uint32 cast cannot perturb the low 12 bits), and the address magnitude is range-checked by the PAIRED ADRP companion (`adr_prel_pg_hi21`, signed-21-bit page delta) — so the ADD itself needs no upper bound. A code-correctness relaxation, byte-pinned host-independently by `Aarch64AddAbsLo12.ResolvesSplusAAboveUint32Max` (`test_aarch64_reloc_formulas.cpp`) + `MachOArm64Exit.MachoArm64ConstAdrpAddLeaHighVaResolvesLowTwelve` (`test_macho_arm64_exit.cpp`), with RED-on-disable demonstrated (restore the `> UINT32_MAX` clause → the high-VA pins fail). The relaxation is confirmed NO-OP for ELF/PE (their VAs are < UINT32_MAX) by the `linux-gcc-release` + `linux-clang-asan` + `linux-arm64-gcc-release` + `windows-msvc-release` legs of run 27192415923 all staying GREEN. | (closed) — dropped the `S+A > UINT32_MAX` clause; kept `S+A ≥ 0` (a negative VA is nonsensical). RUNTIME witness = run 27192415923 `macos-clang-release` #184 (`global_int` macos-arm64 → exit 42). | plan 14 LK6; macOS data-section cycle; runtime witness shared with `D-LK1-MACHO-EXEC-DATA-SECTIONS` |

| `D-FFI-ANGLE-INCLUDE-LINE-SCOPED-HEADER` | A UX pass on include diagnostics, OR a header name legitimately needing multi-token content. Priority: **normal** (fail-loud today — a malformed `#include <foo` is reported, see `tests/tokenizer/test_tokenizer.cpp::FF11MalformedAngleIncludeNoCloserFailsLoud`; only the diagnostic flavor + consumption scope are deferred polish). | A malformed `#include <foo` (no closing `>`) currently runs the coalescing `header-body` mode to EOF and reports the generic `P_UnterminatedString` (matching `string`-body semantics — `header-body` mirrors the `string` body: coalesced `defaultToken`, `endsAt: ">"`, no `popAtNewline`). The long-term polish is a header-specific unterminated flavor (a new `UnterminatedFlavor::Header` → a dedicated `P_*` code) PLUS line-scoped termination (stop the header body at the newline, like `popAtNewline`) so the error is header-specific AND the rest of the file is not consumed past the directive line. Do NOT re-engineer this cycle (scope creep) — the current behavior is consistent established fail-loud, NOT a regression. | FF11 angle-include (`c-subset.lang.json` `include-directive`/`header-body` modes); pairs with the general `popAtNewline` capability; do NOT cite in `src/` (future-work pin only) |
| `D-FFI-CROSS-HEADER-ODR-FIDELITY` | Full C ODR fidelity becomes a goal, OR a corpus surfaces two included headers declaring the same name as DISTINCT symbols. Priority: **normal** (rare — the common case of two headers declaring the SAME `extern` is correctly idempotent). | FF11 goal-2 flags a PROGRAM `extern` conflicting with an INCLUDED header's decl (`S_RedeclaredSymbol`), but NOT the header-vs-header case: two included headers each declaring the same name as DISTINCT symbols currently last-writer-wins silently (idempotent cross-tree `injectBinding` visibility — deliberately not flagged, correct for FF11's program-vs-header scope). Closing work = extend the cross-tree redeclaration check to also flag header-vs-header same-name conflicts (distinct symbols), leaving the program-vs-header path + the same-symbol idempotent case unchanged. | FF11 goal-2 (`semantic_analyzer.cpp` cross-tree redeclaration loop); surfaced by the cycle-21 self-audit; do NOT cite in `src/` (future-work pin only) |
| `D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32` | The first ILP32 (32-bit-pointer) target lands (e.g. i386 / armv7 / wasm32). Today EVERY DSS exec target is 64-bit (x86_64-PE/ELF, arm64-ELF/Mach-O) and LP64 + LLP64 agree on pointer width (8 bytes), so the pointer-width + greatest-width typedefs in the neutral `stdint.json`/`stddef.json` (`intptr_t`/`uintptr_t`/`intmax_t`/`uintmax_t`/`size_t`/`ptrdiff_t`) are correctly i64/u64. Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — the 64-bit-only values are correct for every current target; first surfaced by the p18 SQLite-readiness Cluster G headers cycle as the FIRST consumer of the descriptor typedef path). | When an ILP32 target is added, the pointer-width typedefs (`intptr_t`/`uintptr_t`/`size_t`/`ptrdiff_t`) must become 4-byte for THAT target while staying 8-byte on the 64-bit ones. A single literal hir-text typedef can't express "pointer-width" across both ABIs, so the close is a per-target width resolution: the descriptor declares the typedef as a width-CLASS the semantic phase resolves against the active target's `dataModel`/pointer width (NOT an `if (target == i386)` in the engine — the descriptor/loader declares the width axis, the engine reads it). Pin: an ILP32 target compiles a program asserting `sizeof(intptr_t)==4` while a 64-bit target sees 8. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/{stdint,stddef}.json` ($comment); pairs with `D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH` + `D-FFI-WCHAR-WIDTH` (both "a descriptor baked an ABI/platform width") + `D-FFI-STDINT-LIMIT-MACROS` (the width-dependent *_MAX inherit this); SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-FFI-STDINT-LIMIT-MACROS` | A program references a `<stdint.h>` limit macro — `INT8_MAX`/`INT64_MIN`/`UINT32_MAX`/`SIZE_MAX`/`INTPTR_MAX`/etc. Today the neutral `stdint.json` ships ONLY the typedefs (no `constants` surface), so a direct limit-macro reference fails loud as an undefined identifier (never silent). Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — SQLite's amalgamation mostly self-defines these via `#if !defined(...)`, but a direct reference would need them; first noted p18 Cluster G). | Add a `constants` surface to `stdint.json` carrying the *_MAX/*_MIN integer macros (INT8_MIN=-128 … INT64_MAX=9223372036854775807, the UINT*_MAX, plus SIZE_MAX/PTRDIFF_MIN/PTRDIFF_MAX/INTPTR_*/INTMAX_*), each integer-typed (rides as i64/u64 via the descriptor `constants` mechanism). The pointer-width + greatest-width limits (SIZE_MAX/INTPTR_MAX/INTMAX_MAX) are 64-bit-target values that inherit the ILP32 deferral [[D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32]]. Pin: a program using `INT32_MAX` compiles and the value is byte-exact. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/stdint.json` ($comment); pairs with `D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32` (width-dependent limits) + the descriptor `constants` mechanism (FC14 item-1, cf. `limits.json`); SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-FFI-WCHAR-WIDTH` | A program needs `wchar_t` at its platform-correct width — 16-bit on Windows (PE), 32-bit on POSIX/Linux+macOS (ELF/Mach-O). The neutral `stddef.json` ships `wchar_t = i32` (the Linux+macOS width); on a PE/Windows target the conforming C width is 16-bit. Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — SQLite is UTF-8/`char` internally and uses no `wchar_t`, so the i32 default is correct for the Linux+macOS deliverables and no current corpus exercises it; first noted p18 Cluster G). | Make `wchar_t`'s width per-target (2 bytes on PE/Windows, 4 on ELF/Mach-O) via the SAME per-target width resolution as [[D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32]] (a `dataModel`/format-keyed typedef value the semantic phase resolves against the active target — NOT an `if (format == pe)` in the engine). Pin: a Windows-target program sees `sizeof(wchar_t)==2`, a Linux-target one sees `4`. | cited in `src/dss-config/shippedLibs/stddef.json` ($comment); pairs with `D-FFI-STDINT-PTR-WIDTH-ILP32` + `D-LANG-PLATFORM-DEPENDENT-PRIMITIVE-WIDTH`; SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18) |
| `D-FFI-OFFSETOF-MACRO` | A program references `offsetof(type, member)` from `<stddef.h>`. Today `stddef.json` ships `size_t`/`ptrdiff_t`/`wchar_t`/`NULL` but NOT `offsetof` (a function-like macro — no descriptor surface for it yet), so an `offsetof` reference fails loud. Priority: **normal** (trigger-gated — SQLite uses `offsetof` in a few spots, so this may fire during the SQLite compile; first noted p18 Cluster G). | `offsetof` is the function-like macro `((size_t)&((type*)0)->member)`. | `D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MISCOMPILE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c2 — ROOT CAUSE = INLINING a variadic callee).** A variadic function SILENTLY MISCOMPILED under the RELEASE optimizer pipeline. Minimal repro (`examples`-shaped): `static int vsum(int n, ...){ va_list ap; int acc=0,i; va_start(ap,n); for(i=0;i<n;i=i+1) acc=acc+va_arg(ap,int); va_end(ap); return acc; } int main(void){ return vsum(3,10,13,19); }` → **baseline (debug pipeline) exit 42 (CORRECT); release (`--config=release`) exit 0 (WRONG)** on x86_64-PE (reproduced HEAD 0e3a550, `build/bin/dss/Release`). **Priority: HIGH — correctness-critical, silent miscompile.** BLOCKS SQLite-green RELEASE: SQLite is variadic-heavy (`sqlite3_mprintf`/`sqlite3_snprintf`/`sqlite3VXPrintf`/its test harnesses). ROOT of the blind spot: FC12 shipped the variadic feature BASELINE-ONLY (its corpus carried no `{"shippedPipeline":"release"}` arm), so the optimizer×`va_list` composition was NEVER witnessed — exactly the masked-effectiveness trap the dss-cycle `release`-arm corpus rule exists to prevent. | ✅ (CLOSED) ROOT CAUSE = the INLINER inlined the static single-call variadic callee into `main`; the spliced `va_start` leaves (`VaRegSaveAreaAddr`/`VaOverflowArgAreaAddr`/`VaHomeArgAreaAddr`) bound to MAIN's frame (which never spilled the varargs) → `ap` read garbage. FIX = `inlineLegalityGate` (`src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp`) refuses any callee whose body contains one of those three va_start leaves — the universal "a variadic fn that calls va_start is not inlinable" rule; agnostic (MIR opcodes only), sibling of the `RecvByValueStackParam` refusal. PINS (both red-on-disable): `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp::VariadicCalleeCallingVaStartIsNotInlined` (callsInlined==0) + corpus `examples/c-subset/varargs_inline_release` (release arm exit 42, PE-runnable). ★ Closing this surfaced 2 MORE variadic-release optimizer bugs the FC12 BASELINE-ONLY corpus masked (a CLUSTER, NOT a single bug) → [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI]] + [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-ARGINDEX]]; the broad "add a `release` arm to EVERY variadic example" closure follows each fix (this cycle adds only `varargs_inline_release` — the other arms stay off until their bug lands). | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c2); cited in `src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp` (gate refusal) + `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/varargs_inline_release/`; pairs with `D-OPT7-INLINE-FRAME-SENSITIVE-INTRINSIC` (the hypothetical-intrinsic sibling — va_start in DSS is these dedicated MIR leaves, not an IntrinsicCall) + `D-FFI-DESCRIPTOR-VARIADIC-SIGNATURE` + the FC12 variadic cycle + the dss-cycle `release`-arm corpus discipline |
| `D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c3) — was the variadic SYMPTOM of a GENERAL Mem2Reg bug; fixed together as [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]].** Compiling `examples/c-subset/varargs_win64_sum` under RELEASE aborted FAIL-LOUD `Mem2Reg fatal: phi ... has no reaching value from predecessor`. ★ The c3 PROBE OVERTURNED the scope: it is NOT Win64/variadic-specific — the trigger is the `int iv = va_arg(ap,int); double dv = va_arg(ap,double);` LOOP-BODY-LOCALS, and a minimal NON-variadic `int f(int n){int t=0,i=0;while(i<n){int iv=i*2;t=t+iv;i=i+1;}return t;}` reproduces the IDENTICAL fatal. The variadic example was just the FIRST to exercise it under release (FC12 shipped the variadic corpus baseline-only). | ✅ (CLOSED) FIXED by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]] (semi-pruned SSA — see that row for the mechanism). `varargs_win64_sum` gained a `{"shippedPipeline":"release"}` arm (exit 39, was Mem2Reg-fatal); the general witness is `examples/c-subset/loop_body_local`. | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3); subsumed by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]]; pairs with [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MISCOMPILE]] (the inlining sibling) + [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-ARGINDEX]] (the still-open 3rd cluster member) |
| `D-OPT-MEM2REG-DEAD-PHI-PRUNE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c3 — the COMPLETE fix; HIGH, GENERAL Mem2Reg correctness bug).** Under the RELEASE pipeline Mem2Reg ABORTED FAIL-LOUD (`phi at block ... has no reaching value from predecessor`) whenever a promoted alloca got a DEAD phi at an IDF block where it was not LIVE but its incoming was undefined. TWO classes: (1) a loop-BODY-LOCAL (`while(){ int x=expr; use(x); }`, dead at the header) — the first-found symptom [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]]; (2) the SUBTLER NESTED-LOOP case — an inner counter `j` re-initialized each OUTER iteration is LIVE across the inner back-edge yet DEAD at the OUTER header. Class (2) (and a single loop whose body contains an `if`-merge) crashes with ZERO body-locals → an ENORMOUS class of ordinary C (nested loops saturate SQLite). The c3 pr-review's RUNTIME battery caught (2) after the initial semi-pruned commit (ecf40c3) only handled (1) — the green-but-incomplete trap; upgraded to the complete fix the same cycle. | ✅ (CLOSED) FIX = FULLY-PRUNED SSA (Choi/Cytron/Sarkar) in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp`: place a phi for alloca A at IDF block S ONLY IF A is LIVE-IN at S (a backward live-in dataflow: `live_in[B]=use[B] ∪ (live_out[B]\def[B])`, use=upward-exposed Load, def=Store, alloca-site NOT a def). Strictly stronger than semi-pruned (upward-exposure): a name DEAD at one IDF block but live elsewhere (the nested counter) is pruned THERE specifically. PROVABLY SAFE: every KEPT phi is at a block where A is live → a needed merge is never pruned (no miscompile, verified by a base==release battery: diamond/induction/nested/triple-nested/body-local-live-across all correct on both pipelines). PRESERVES fail-loud: a genuine uninitialized read IS live-in at its use → phi kept → still aborts (verified). PINS (red-on-disable): `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp::{LoopBodyLocalAllocaNeedsNoPhi, NestedLoopInnerCounterNoOuterHeaderPhi}` + corpus `examples/c-subset/{loop_body_local (exit 20), nested_loop_release (exit 4)}` release arms. Agnostic (MIR/SSA only). | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3); cited in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp` (the live-in gate) + `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/nested_loop_release/`; subsumes [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI]] (class 1); pairs with the Choi/Cytron/Sarkar pruned-SSA literature |
| `D-OPT-MEM2REG-LOOP-BODY-LOCAL-DEAD-PHI` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3) — ★ SUPERSEDED by [[D-OPT-MEM2REG-DEAD-PHI-PRUNE]] (the COMPLETE fix).** The SEMI-PRUNED fix this row first described (commit ecf40c3, gate phi placement on UPWARD-EXPOSURE) was INSUFFICIENT: the c3 pr-review's runtime battery found NESTED loops still crashed (a name DEAD at one IDF block but live elsewhere — upward-exposure cannot prune that); upgraded to FULLY-PRUNED (live-in) the SAME cycle. The loop-body-local class IS fixed by the general fix. Original c3 record (the first-found symptom):** GENERAL Mem2Reg correctness bug — HIGH, was masked. Under the RELEASE pipeline, Mem2Reg ABORTED FAIL-LOUD (`phi at block ... has no reaching value from predecessor ... uninit/unreachable input`) on ANY function with a local declared AND used entirely inside a LOOP BODY (`while (...) { int x = expr; use(x); }`) — an enormous, ordinary class of C (it would have blocked vast swaths of SQLite). ROOT: minimal (un-pruned) SSA placed a DEAD phi for the block-local at the loop HEADER (the body-Store's iterated dominance frontier reaches the header via the back-edge); that phi's entry-predecessor incoming was genuinely undefined (the slot was never stored before the loop) → the rename walk's empty-stack guard aborted. Surfaced (re-scoped) from the variadic symptom [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI]] by the c3 probe (a non-variadic `while(){int iv=...}` reproduces it). Was masked because release-arm corpus examples never declared a loop-body-local (the dss-cycle masked-effectiveness trap, again). | ✅ (CLOSED) FIX = SEMI-PRUNED SSA (Briggs/Cooper) in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp`: gate phi PLACEMENT on UPWARD-EXPOSURE — only place a phi for an alloca read-before-written in SOME block (a "global" name). A block-local (Store-before-Load in its block) is not upward-exposed → no dead phi. PROVABLY SAFE: a global alloca's placement is BYTE-IDENTICAL to before (induction vars / diamond joins unchanged), so the fix ONLY removes the spurious dead phis. CRUCIALLY PRESERVES fail-loud: a genuine uninitialized read (`int x; if(c) x=1; use(x)`) IS upward-exposed at the use → stays global → still gets its phi → still aborts on the undefined path (verified: that case still fatals). PINS: `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp::LoopBodyLocalAllocaNeedsNoPhi` (induction var=1 phi, body-local=0 phi; red-on-disable = the pass aborts) + corpus `examples/c-subset/loop_body_local` (release arm exit 20, PE-runnable) + the `varargs_win64_sum` release arm (exit 39). Agnostic (MIR-only, no identity branch). | CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 c3); cited in `src/opt/passes/mem2reg.cpp` (the semi-pruned gate) + `tests/opt/test_mem2reg.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/loop_body_local/`; pairs with [[D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-MEM2REG-PHI]] (the variadic symptom it subsumes) + the Cytron-Ferrante / Briggs-Cooper SSA literature |
| `D-OPT-VARIADIC-RELEASE-ARGINDEX` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-25 (p18 Cluster G c4) — ROOT CAUSE = DCE; GENERAL (not variadic), the LAST cluster member.** Compiling `examples/c-subset/varargs_overflow_fixed_stack` under RELEASE aborted FAIL-LOUD `I_ArgIndexOutOfRange: argIndex 6 >= physical-arg count 2`. ★ The c4 probe BISECTED it to **Dce** (without `Dce` it compiles) and re-scoped it GENERAL: `pick(a,b,c,d,e,f,g,...)` uses only `a` + `g`, so DCE elided the 5 unused param `Arg`s → only 2 `Arg`s survived, but the still-live `Arg(6)` (g, the 7th int → SysV stack) kept its physical ordinal 6 → the MirVerifier's FC7 count-based bound (`argIndex < count(Arg)`, valid only while every Arg survives) spuriously rejected it. A NON-variadic `int f(int a..g){return a+g;}` reproduces it identically (any fn with an unused param before a used high-ordinal one). The codegen was always correct (ordinals preserved); only the verifier over-rejected. | ✅ (CLOSED) FIX = treat `Arg` as an ABI-parameter ROOT in DCE (`isSideEffectRoot` in `src/opt/passes/dce.cpp` returns true for `MirOpcode::Arg`): a parameter is part of the fixed ABI signature, never dead code (LLVM models params as non-instruction `Argument` roots) — so DCE never elides an unused param's `Arg`, holding `count(Arg)` == the physical-arg count the verifier bounds against. | `D-CSUBSET-DESCRIPTOR-TYPEDEF-POINTER-DECL` | ★ **FIRED — discovered 2026-06-25 (p18 SQLite-readiness Cluster G c1, while strengthening the `shipped_int_headers` corpus with a NULL witness).** A DESCRIPTOR-injected typedef name (from a shipped-header JSON descriptor — `int32_t`/`uint8_t`/`size_t`/…) used in POINTER-DECLARATOR position (`int32_t* p` / `size_t *p`) is NOT recognized as a type-name by the PARSER, so `int32_t * p` parses as a MULTIPLICATION expression (`int32_t` × `p`) → fails loud `S_UndeclaredIdentifier` (p) + `S_TypeMismatch` (initializer). ROOT: descriptor typedefs are injected SEMANTICALLY (post-parse, into cuRoot by `semantic_analyzer`), so the parser's `T * x` declaration-vs-multiply disambiguation never learns them. CONTRAST (all verified this cycle): a USER `typedef int myint; myint* p` WORKS (the parser sees the typedef decl → type-name visible); a BUILTIN `int* p` WORKS (keyword); and descriptor typedefs WORK in the UNAMBIGUOUS positions — scalar decl (`int32_t r`) + cast (`(int32_t)n`) — which need no parser type-name table. Only the pointer-declarator ambiguity exposes it. **FAILS LOUD (never a silent miscompile).** Priority: **normal — SQLite blast-radius UNMEASURED** (SQLite mostly uses its OWN amalgamation typedefs [`u8`/`u32`/`sqlite3_int64`, parser-visible → fine], but a direct `size_t *`/`uint8_t *` on a stdint/stddef typedef would mis-parse; re-probe sqlite3.c for descriptor-typedef pointer usage to set the real priority). | Make descriptor typedef-names parser-visible BEFORE the `T * x` disambiguation. Two designs (likely a §B fork): **(a)** pre-scan the source's `#include <...>` set → resolve descriptors → SEED the parser's type-name table before parsing (today includes resolve POST-parse in `import_resolver`, so this needs include-set-at-parse-time — the classic C lexer-hack ordering); **(b)** make the declaration-vs-multiply disambiguation SEMANTIC — speculatively parse both, resolve by whether `T` names a type in the semantic scope (incl. descriptor injections). Pin: `#include <stdint.h>\nint32_t g=42; int main(){ int32_t* p=&g; return (int)*p; }` compiles + exits 42, RED-on-disable. | discovered by p18 Cluster G c1 (`examples/c-subset/shipped_int_headers/main.c` references it in a comment — examples/ is NOT anchor-guard-scanned, so informational); pairs with the FC14 descriptor typedef-injection path (`semantic_analyzer.cpp` inject) + the c-subset declaration-vs-expression speculative parse + `D-PARSE-IDENTIFIER-KIND-HARDCODED-VS-CONFIG`; SQLite-readiness Cluster G (p18); do NOT cite in `src/` yet (discovered-gap pin) |

| `D-OPT7-INLINE-FRAME-SENSITIVE-INTRINSIC` | The first FRAME-SENSITIVE intrinsic is registered/emitted by a frontend — a `va_start`/`va_arg`, `frameaddress`/`returnaddress`, `stacksave`/`stackrestore`, or `setjmp`-class intrinsic whose semantics depend on the ENCLOSING function's stack frame. Priority: **trigger-gated** (do NOT build until a frame-sensitive intrinsic exists — today NO shipped frontend emits ANY intrinsic, and the only known intrinsics [`sqrt`, `textureSample`] are pure/frame-insensitive, so the MIR inliner's cycle-29 blanket IntrinsicCall admission is correct; building an inline-safety attribute now would be a consumer-less SPECULATIVE mechanism — the §E#5 over-engineering violation). | OPT7 cycle 29 (2026-06-05) made `inlineLegalityGate` blanket-ADMIT IntrinsicCall-bearing callees (`D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` arm d). That is SSA-correct for every frame-INSENSITIVE intrinsic but would MISCOMPILE a frame-sensitive one: an inlined `va_start`/`frameaddress` binds to the CALLER's frame, not the callee's. The MIR inliner sees only the bare intrinsic id (no semantics), so it cannot distinguish safe from unsafe. Closing work = add a per-intrinsic INLINE-SAFETY attribute to `HirIntrinsicDescriptor` (`src/hir/hir_intrinsic_registry.hpp` — e.g. `frameSensitive`/`inlineSafe`, registration-driven, default inline-safe), thread it into the MIR `IntrinsicCall` (a side-table or inst flag carried from `hir_to_mir` lowering since the MIR id is bare), and gate the inliner to REFUSE a callee containing a frame-sensitive IntrinsicCall. Pin: a frame-sensitive intrinsic in a callee → NOT inlined (`callsInlined==0`), RED-on-disable; the tripwire updated to register the new intrinsic + assert the gate refuses it. | plan 22 §2.9 OPT7; cited in `src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp` (gate comments at the IntrinsicCall admission + rule 5) + `src/opt/passes/inlining.hpp` (header doc rule 5); the fail-loud tripwire is `tests/hir/test_hir_lowering_c_subset.cpp::NoShippedConstructLowersToIntrinsic`; follows on from `D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` arm (d) |

| `D-OPT7-MULTIBLOCK-SPLICE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-05** (OPT7 cycle 2). The inliner now splices a GENERAL MULTI-BLOCK LEAF callee (cycle 1 was single-block-only). `inlineLegalityGate` LIFTED the `funcBlockCount(callee) != 1` refusal but keeps the leaf scan across ALL callee blocks (no `Call`/`IntrinsicCall` anywhere). Because the `tryRewrite` hook (1 Call → 1 value, mid-block-fill) structurally cannot create blocks, a function with any multi-block target is rebuilt by a new `MultiBlockInliner` (`src/opt/passes/inlining.cpp`): per original caller block kept as a branch target (`blockMap_`); the call-site block SPLIT at the Call (a fresh CONTINUATION block holds the after-Call insts); the callee CFG CLONED in RPO (fresh block+inst ids, shared callee→caller `local` map); each cloned `Return` rewritten to `Br(continuation)` collecting (value, cloned-pred) edges; a RETURN-MERGE PHI in the continuation joins them (elided to the single value for a 1-return callee; void callee → no Phi). StructCfMarker RE-DERIVED to `Linear` for every cloned + continuation block (SimplifyCfg cycle-9 precedent) — a clone of the callee's `EntryBlock`/`ExitBlock` would violate the verifier's entry/exit rules, and transplanting If/Loop marker COUNTS would break caller marker-parity; `Linear` is parity-neutral. Caller `Phi` incomings redirect `pred` through `blockExitMap_` (the last continuation of a split chain). **Proven**: runtime corpus `examples/c-subset/multiblock_inline/` (`pick(x){if(x>0)return 7;return 9;}`; `main` = `pick(1)+pick(0)` = 16) with an `optimizedPipelines:["Inlining"]` arm == baseline 16; **REGRESSION-PROVEN RED** — mis-wiring the merge to always pick the first return edge makes the optimized arm fail to compile (the then-clone value doesn't dominate the else→continuation path → MirVerifier rejects via verify-after-every-pass → differential ASSERT fires). MIR-tier pins in `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp`: `MultiBlockLeafCalleeIsInlined` (Call gone + caller block count +4 [3 clones + 1 cont] + exactly 1 merge Phi + merge-Phi incomings CORRECTLY value↔pred paired [`instBlock(value)==pred` for the 7-from-then + 9-from-else edges; a swapped incoming → RED, catching a mis-merge the MIR tier alone would miss] + verifier-clean, RED-on-disable) + (at cycle-2 time) `MultiBlockNonLeafCalleeIsNotInlined` (scope boundary — **SUPERSEDED in cycle 27**: that scope boundary was the multi-block leaf restriction, which `D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` cycle 27 LIFTED; the test was flipped to `MultiBlockNonLeafCalleeIsInlined`, and a multi-block non-leaf callee now inlines). **Robustness gate (review fold 2026-06-05):** `inlineLegalityGate` ALSO refuses a leaf callee with NO RETURNING PATH (no `Return` in any block; every path ends in `Unreachable` — e.g. `int f(){ while(1){} }`). Without the refusal the splice routes each callee `Return` to a continuation block; a never-returning callee leaves that continuation predecessor-less → the MirVerifier (run after every pass) rejects the module → an otherwise-valid program becomes a build error UNDER inlining. Refusing keeps the Call out-of-line so the program compiles (conservative, never a miscompile). Pinned by `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp::NonReturningLeafCalleeIsNotInlined` (multi-block entry→`Unreachable` leaf → callsInlined==0, Call survives, module still verifies; RED-on-disable: removing `if (!hasReturn) return nullopt;` admits it → the splice's `mapCallerValue` fail-loud aborts the build). | (closed) | plan 22 §2.9 OPT7; cited in `src/opt/passes/inlining.{hpp,cpp}` + `tests/opt/test_inlining.cpp` + `examples/c-subset/multiblock_inline/`; pairs with `D-OPT7-MULTIBLOCK-SPLICE-PHI` (callee-Phi deferral) + `D-OPT7-INLINE-LEGALITY-GATE` |
| `D-OPT7-MULTIBLOCK-SPLICE-PHI` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13** (OPT7 callee-Phi cycle — §B design brief signed off, then built to the bar). `inlineLegalityGate`'s callee-`Phi` refusal is DROPPED (TOTAL — no shape gate replaces it); `MultiBlockInliner` now CLONES callee Phis via a DEFERRED-incoming-flush, a sibling of the return-merge `returnEdges` with a DISJOINT map (they compose without interference): a placeholder `dst_.addPhi(instType)` is emitted in the RPO clone loop (recorded into `deferredCalleePhis` + `local`, so later insts referencing the phi resolve), and AFTER the whole clone loop each incoming is flushed — the VALUE remapped via the shared `local` map (`mapCalleeOperand`), the PRED via the `calleeBlockMap` (callee-block→caller-block clone), with a fail-loud `std::abort` on a pred-not-in-clone-map (structurally unreachable — every callee block is pre-created in phase 1). The deferral is LOAD-BEARING for a LOOP-phi: the back-edge incoming VALUE is defined later in RPO (in the latch), so an inline flush would hit `mapCalleeOperand`'s def-before-use abort — flushing after the loop (when `local` is complete) is what makes it resolve. The `emitCalleeInst` Phi arm is KEPT as a defensive fail-loud guard (a Phi is handled in the clone loop and never reaches it; rationale comment corrected). | `D-MERGE-UNREACHABLE-BLOCK` | Cycle 25 Stage B (2026-06-05): `mergeCuMirs` (`src/mir/merge/mir_merge.cpp`, `FunctionCloner::clone`) clones each surviving function's REACHABLE CFG — it pre-creates every natural block then fills in RPO from the entry (a valid def-before-use order for SSA). A pre-created block NOT reached by RPO (genuinely unreachable from the entry) is left unfilled, which the `MirBuilder`'s every-block-must-be-filled invariant would abort on at `finish()`; the cloner instead FAILS LOUD first (named abort) with attribution. This is correct for the merge's real inputs because the **c-subset frontend does not emit entry-unreachable blocks** (every block it lowers is reachable from the function entry; DCE, when the active pipeline runs it, additionally removes any dead block), and the hand-built tests are likewise all-reachable — so the unfilled-block case never arises today and the limitation is unobservable. The reachable-only assumption is NOT load-bearing for soundness, though: the **fail-loud abort is the actual backstop** — if a future input ever carried an unreachable block, the merge aborts with attribution rather than emitting a malformed function, so it is never a silent miscompile. Trigger = the first merge input carrying an unreachable block (e.g. a future frontend that emits an entry-unreachable block, or a debug/identity pipeline that runs no DCE on input that happens to contain one). Priority: **normal** (fail-loud today; never a silent miscompile). | Either (a) run DCE / dead-block elimination on each CU's MIR BEFORE the merge so only reachable blocks remain, OR (b) extend `FunctionCloner` to clone unreachable blocks too (fill them after the RPO pass in natural order; their intra-block SSA is self-contained, and cross-block operands into a dead block can't be live, so a second natural-order fill pass over the unfilled set suffices). Byte-identical for the shipped corpus (arm64/x86_64-darwin `headerAndCmds` ~840 ≪ `segmentPageSize` ⇒ `impliedOffset == textFileOff`, check passes silently — 394 ctest green, no corpus change). Pinned RED-on-disable by `MachOExecWriter.SchemaTextVaInconsistentWithTextFileOffFailsLoud` — a synthetic exec format (`loadFromText`, VA = `pageZeroSize + 2×segmentPageSize` = 0x100002000, congruent so validate ACCEPTS it but the textFileOff inequality fires) + trivial module ⇒ encode aborts (`bytes.empty()`); toggle-verified (revert ⇒ test fails). The two walker call sites route through the ONE tested chokepoint helper (§A.5 option-a by-construction coverage; static path end-to-end pinned, dynamic path's identical call verified by independent review). — *Original row (audit trail):* The Mach-O exec walker reads `__text.virtualAddress` from the format JSON and trusts it equals `pageZeroSize + alignUp(headerAndCmds, segmentPageSize)` (i.e. `textSecOffsetInSeg == textFileOff`). For the arm64-darwin corpus this holds because headerAndCmds (~864 bytes) ≪ segmentPageSize (16384), so textFileOff = 0x4000 and the shipped VA is 0x100004000. The walker's congruence guard (`macho.cpp` `(sectionVa - pageZeroSize) % segmentPageSize`) + validate() catch a NON-congruent VA loud, but NEITHER enforces the stronger `== textFileOff` equality (which is module-dependent — headerAndCmds depends on the load commands of the module being linked, not the schema alone). So a future format whose load commands exceed `segmentPageSize` (many dylibs / a huge symtab) would push textFileOff past the hardcoded VA and emit an inconsistent section addr. Strictly BETTER than the pre-16K state (headroom grew from 4096 → 16384 bytes). Priority: **trigger-gated / low** (first darwin-exec whose header+load-commands exceed segmentPageSize). | Compute `sectionVa = pageZeroSize + textFileOff` in the walker (making the schema `virtualAddress` advisory / a cross-check) OR add an encode-time `textSecOffsetInSeg == textFileOff` fail-loud assertion. Pin with a synthetic darwin-exec carrying enough load commands to exceed one segmentPageSize. | `D-LK10-ENTRY-MACHO-EXIT`; `src/link/format/macho.cpp` (the sectionVa derivation); future-work pin (do NOT cite in src) |
| `D-LK7-CODESIGN-PAGESIZE-OVERFLOW-HARDENING` | The ad-hoc codesign `pageSize` is now schema-validated to a power-of-two in **[4096, 65536]** (`object_format_schema_json.cpp` — closes the reachable `pageSize:1` slot-table u32 overflow: `nCodeSlots*32` could wrap on a multi-GiB binary; pinned by `PageSizeBelowFloorFailsLoud`/`AboveCeilingFailsLoud`). One RESIDUAL truly-unreachable overflow remains: `codeSlotCount`'s `(codeLimit + pageSize - 1u)` could wrap in u32 only if `codeLimit` is within `pageSize` of `UINT32_MAX` (a >~4 GiB signed binary) — and `macho.cpp` already fails loud if `codeSigFileOff > u32 max` before the builder runs, AND the `sig.size() != reservation` guard fails loud on any size disagreement, so it is fail-loud-protected + outside this compiler's operating range. Priority: **trigger-gated** (a >~4 GiB output binary reaches the codesign builder). | Widen `codeSlotCount` + `codeDirectoryLength` to compute in `std::uint64_t` with an explicit `> u32 max` fail-loud on the final blob length; OR raise the pageSize floor further. So a DSS macho64-arm64-darwin-exec could be byte-pinned but **could not RUN** on `macos-latest` → the §A.5 runtime closure is unreachable (exactly the FFI-ISEL over-claim trap). Priority: **high** (the active prerequisite; runs next cycle with fresh context). | `D-AP2-COMPILATION-CONTEXT` | Plan 06 AP2 (2026-06-09): AP2 VALIDATES the artifact profile (fail-loud `D_ArtifactProfileNotSupported`) and delegates the build, but does NOT thread the resolved profile to codegen — there is no path to do so today (`compileFiles`/`compileUnits` → `runCusToTargets` build `CompileOptions` internally with no profile field; adding one would be a dead knob, the plan-lock Contest-2 finding). Plan 06 §2.3.4 stamps the profile onto a **CompilationContext**. **REPOINTED 2026-06-09 (AP3):** AP3 did NOT thread the profile to codegen — a §B + the AP3 plan-lock established that **NO shipped language/profile has a codegen effect the chosen `(target:format)` spec doesn't already encode** (cli→exec-format→trampoline; lib→dll/dyn-format; staticlib→relocatable/archive), so threading-to-codegen now would be a DEAD KNOB. AP3 instead landed the profile's first REAL effect = the **profile↔format compatibility gate** (`D_ArtifactProfileFormatMismatch`, driver-side). The codegen-threading therefore stays deferred — its trigger is NOT "AP3" but **the first profile that drives a NON-format-redundant codegen difference** (a `gui` profile, or a `cli`-vs-`gui` split within ONE format — different entry-symbol + PE subsystem from the same exec format). Until such a consumer exists, threading the profile to codegen has no reader → would be a speculative build. Priority: **trigger-gated (do NOT build until a non-format-redundant profile consumer lands; e.g. gui codegen)**. | When a non-format-redundant profile consumer lands: introduce the profile-carrying context (or thread `artifactProfile` through the driver→pipeline call chain) so codegen reads it; pin with an interface test that codegen sees the resolved profile + a runtime/behavioral pin that the profile changes the artifact (e.g. subsystem/entry-symbol). | plan 06 §2.3/§2.4 + §5 (AP3/AP4); cited in `src/program/program.cpp` + `src/program/project_config.hpp`; the AP2 plan-lock Contest-2 + the AP3 §B (compatibility-gate-not-threading) |
| `D-AP2-TARGET-NAME-DEFAULT-FORMAT` | Plan 06 AP2 (2026-06-09): the project-config `targets[]` are `"<targetName>:<formatName>"` specs (the as-built driver convention, validated downstream by `D_InvalidTargetSpec`). The §2.2 example uses BARE target names (`"linux-x86_64"`); resolving a bare name to a default object-format is deferred. Trigger: first project config (or UX decision) that wants bare target names with an inferred default format. | `D-HIR-LOOP-BODY-ONLY-RETURN-DOUBLE-ATTACH` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13 (pre-FC5 deferral mini-arc).** Root cause was NOT loop-specific: `maybeAppendImplicitReturnZero` (src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp) re-wrapped the body's ALREADY-PARENTED children via `makeBlock(oldKids+ret)`, and `makeBlock`→`addParent` aborts on a re-parented child (HIR is immutable) — so ANY non-empty non-terminating `main` crashed (the infinite-loop shapes AND `int main(){int x;x=1;}` are instances; the empty `int main(){}` survived only because oldKids was empty). FIX: immutability-safe nest — wrap the (unparented) body block + the synthetic return in a fresh outer block (`makeBlock({body,ret})`), never re-parenting children; the `addParent` guard is untouched. Infinite-loop mains now compile + run (the dead `return 0` is dropped by the MIR unreachable-prune); 274/274 ctest; corpus `infinite_loop_return_main` (exit 5) + `for_inf_return_main` (exit 9) + 2 HIR pins; red-on-disable demonstrated. The SEPARATE non-`main` infinite-loop over-rejection is `D-HIR-INFINITE-LOOP-NOT-TERMINATING` (next in the mini-arc). *(Original status, preserved:)* **OPEN (surfaced 2026-06-13 by the MIR unreachable-prune cycle's test-shape exploration — PRE-EXISTING; the prune diff touches NO src/hir/ or src/mir/lowering loop builder). Priority: normal.** A loop whose body is ONLY a return/seal (`while(1){return X;}`, `do{return X;}while(c);`, `for(;;){return X;}`) trips a HirBuilder fatal `addParent: HirNodeId=N already has a parent (double-attach)` during HIR construction — the tree-shaped-HIR structural guard fires on a VALID-C shape. Orthogonal to the MIR prune (upstream, in HIR build); the prune's loop-orphan coverage is instead via `for(i=0;i<10;i=i+1){return 11;}` (update-block orphan). | Root-cause the double-attach in HirBuilder for a loop body that seals immediately (a node re-parented between the body slot and a synthesized continue/exit edge); pin with the three loop-only-return shapes compiling + running. | hir_to_mir.cpp loop lowering; HirBuilder `addParent` guard; surfaced by the prune cycle; future-work pin (do NOT cite in src) |
| `D-HIR-DEAD-CODE-AFTER-RETURN-REJECTED` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13 (pre-FC5 deferral mini-arc).** Relaxed the HIR verifier's dead-code-after-terminator rejection: `checkBlockTermination` now emits a NEW `H_UnreachableCode` (0xF00D) WARNING instead of the `H_VerifierFailure` ERROR, so `verify()` passes and `return X; <dead>;` COMPILES — the dead statement reaches MIR, lowers via the Block-lowering fresh-dead-block, and is dropped by the unreachable-prune (runtime = the reachable `return X`). ISO-C-aligned (warn, don't reject). Scope: ONLY `checkBlockTermination`; the non-void-fall-through `H_VerifierFailure` ERROR (`checkReturnCompleteness`) is UNTOUCHED (still rejects). Priority: normal (matters for the full-C / FC arc).** Statements after a `return` in the same block (`return 42; return 7;`) are REJECTED by the HIR verifier (`H0003`, "statement is unreachable") BEFORE MIR — so the MIR prune is not their guard. | `D-HIR-INFINITE-LOOP-NOT-TERMINATING` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-13 (pre-FC5 deferral mini-arc).** Implemented the documented design: `lowerWhile`/`lowerFor` (cst_to_hir.cpp) now wrap a PROVABLY-INFINITE loop (const-truthy/absent condition via the shared `evalCstConstInt` const-eval, AND no `break` reachable in this loop's own frame — a frame-respecting body scan that does NOT descend into nested loops/switches) as `Block{ loop, Unreachable }`, so `pathTerminates` (recursing to the Block's last child) recognizes the function terminates. `int f(){while(1){return 5;}}` now compiles + runs (exit 5); `for(;;)`/`do-while(1)` likewise. NEGATIVE-pinned (no false positive = no miscompile): a breakable `while(1){if(x)break;}`, `while(0)`, `while(x)`, and a nested-inner-break are NOT wrapped. A statement-position `Unreachable` gained MIR lowering (`addUnreachable`), and MIR Block-lowering opens a fresh dead block for any sibling after a mid-block seal (dropped by the MIR unreachable-prune) — which INCIDENTALLY fixed a pre-existing latent crash of `<both-arms-return-if> <sibling>` (`int f(){if(x){return 1;}else{return 2;} return 99;}`), now pinned (corpus `nonmain_if_both_ret_dead_tail`). `pathTerminates`/the verifier/H0003/the inliner UNTOUCHED. 280/280 ctest; red-on-disable pinned. *(Original status, preserved:)* **OPEN (surfaced 2026-06-13 by the pre-FC5 deferral mini-arc — PRE-EXISTING). Priority: normal (next in the mini-arc, before FC5).** `pathTerminates` (the HIR verifier-substrate SSOT, src/hir/hir_verifier.hpp) is deliberately CONSERVATIVE — it does NOT count a loop body as terminating; the doc says lowering should append an `Unreachable` after a PROVABLY-INFINITE loop to make the structural answer match the dynamic one, but that step was NEVER implemented (no Unreachable-synthesis in cst_to_hir.cpp). Consequence: a non-`main` function whose only exit is inside a provably-infinite loop (`int f(){ while(1){ return 5; } }`, `for(;;){...}`) is OVER-REJECTED by the non-void-return-completeness check (pathTerminates(body)==false). Valid ISO C. (`main` is unaffected as of 2026-06-13: the implicit-return-0 nest gives it a terminating return; this anchor is the NON-`main` case.) Sibling of `D-HIR-DEAD-CODE-AFTER-RETURN-REJECTED` (both are pathTerminates/termination over-rejections of valid C). | Implement the documented design: detect a provably-infinite loop (constant-truthy or absent condition AND no `break`/`goto` that can exit this loop's frame) in cst_to_hir lowering and append a synthetic `Unreachable` after it, so `pathTerminates` recognizes the function terminates (the MIR unreachable-prune drops the resulting dead block). Pin: `int f(){while(1){return 5;}}` called from main → exit 5; a breakable loop still requires a real return after it. | src/hir/hir_verifier.hpp `pathTerminates` doc (the unimplemented append-`Unreachable` contract); src/hir/lowering/cst_to_hir.cpp loop lowering; the non-void-completeness check in hir_verifier.cpp; sibling `D-HIR-DEAD-CODE-AFTER-RETURN-REJECTED`; downstream owner `D-MIR-UNREACHABLE-PRUNE-NORMALIZE`; future-work pin (do NOT cite in src) |
| `D-PP-FUNCTION-LIKE-MACRO` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-19 (FC13 cycle 2 — function-like macros).** The config-selected C preprocessor now implements function-like `#define F(a,b) ...` definitions AND invocations over the common direct-invocation subset of §6.10.3 (full hide-set deferred → `D-PP-MACRO-HIDESET-PRECISE`). `MacroExpander::handleDefine` parses the parameter list (comma-separated `Word` params, adjacency `(`-after-name detection on raw spans, empty `()` ⇒ zero params); the redefinition-compatibility check compares kind + params + replacement text (`sameDefinition`). The cycle-1 token-by-token `expandInto` was reworked into a STREAM expander `expand(std::span<Token const>, painting, depth)` (object- AND function-like uniformly): a function-like name is an invocation ONLY if the next significant token is the configured `(` (else emitted verbatim, §6.10.3p10); `collectArgs` collects paren-balance-tracked arguments (depth via the configured open/close paren; a depth-1 comma separates, the depth-0 close ends; trivia-trimmed); each argument is PRE-EXPANDED (`expand` in the current paint context, the invoked macro not yet painted, §6.10.3.1); `substitute` maps param-name tokens → pre-expanded arg tokens; the result is RESCANNED with the macro painted blue (§6.10.3.4 self-reference freeze). Zero-PARAM `M()` is normalized to zero args at the call site. FAIL-LOUD: arity mismatch + unterminated invocation (`P_PreprocessorMacroArgument`, new 0x0017); duplicate parameter + malformed param list (`P_PreprocessorDirective`); VARIADIC `#define V(...)` (`P_PreprocessorUnsupported` → `D-PP-VARIADIC-MACRO`, deferred). AGNOSTIC: the close-paren is config (`preprocess.functionLikeCloseToken`, mirroring the opener — `)` lexes as core `Punctuation`, so it MUST come from config). The cycle-1 `FunctionLikeMacroDefinitionFailsLoud` test was FLIPPED to `FunctionLikeMacroSimpleInvocationExpands`; 12 new function-like unit tests (nested, arg-is-macro pre-expansion, arity, verbatim-name, mixing, recursive-freeze, empty/zero-paren, variadic, dup-param, unterminated) + runnable 4-target corpus `examples/c-subset/preprocessor_function_macros` (exit 42). 331 ctest; object-macro tests + corpus unregressed; RED-on-disable demonstrated (neutering `substitute`). *(Original status, preserved:)* FC13 cycle 1 (2026-06-19): the config-selected C preprocessor (`src/analysis/preprocess/`) implements OBJECT-like `#define`/`#undef` only. A FUNCTION-like macro DEFINITION (`#define F(x) ...` - a `(` immediately adjacent to the macro name) is recognized and FAILS LOUD (`P_PreprocessorUnsupported`, `MacroExpander::handleDefine`), never silently passed through as object-like (which would mis-expand). Priority: **normal (cycle 2)** - the function-like macro feature (parameter capture, argument substitution; the `#`/`##` operators are SEPARATE = FC15) is the next preprocessor cycle. | Build function-like macro definition + invocation: parse the parameter list, capture call-site arguments (paren-balanced), substitute parameters into the replacement, then rescan. Pin: `#define F(x) ((x)+1)` + `F(2)` expands to `((2)+1)`; arity mismatch fails loud. Closing test in `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp` (today `FunctionLikeMacroDefinitionFailsLoud` pins the fail-loud guard - flip it to expand-correctly when the feature lands). | plan 23 FC13; `tests/analysis/preprocess/test_preprocessor.cpp`; successor cycle 2 |
| `D-PP-MACRO-HIDESET-PRECISE` | ✅ **CLOSED 2026-06-19 (FC13 cycle 4 — the precise per-token hide set).** The recursion-scoped blue-PAINT set was REPLACED by Prosser's precise per-token hide set (the standard realization of C §6.10.3.4) — within FC13's no-`#`/`##` scope this now realizes the FULL §6.10.3.4, not merely the cycle-2/3-softened "common direct-invocation subset of §6.10.3". `Token` is a 16B trivially-copyable POD that cannot carry a set, so the expansion WORKING set is a wrapper `struct ExpToken { Token tok; HideSet hide; }` where `HideSet = shared_ptr<set<string> const>` (IMMUTABLE-once-built → copies are a refcount bump, every token of one replacement shares the SAME set object; a null pointer is the canonical EMPTY hide set, so the parser-bound body lifts in with `nullptr` and pays no allocation; `std::set` makes the hot intersection/union a linear merge). `run` lifts `vector<Token>` → `vector<ExpToken>` (empty hide sets), runs `expand`, drops hide sets back to `vector<Token>`. `expand` is now a SPLICE-RESCAN cursor (no longer isolated recursion): on each expansion it splices the produced tokens — each carrying its computed hide set — back over the consumed `[i,past)` region of the working set and rescans from the splice point, so a function-like name and a `(` that become adjacent only ACROSS the replacement/parent boundary RE-PAIR. A token (name M) expands iff `M ∉ hideset(T)`. OBJECT-like M: replacement tokens carry `hideset(T) ∪ {M}`. FUNCTION-like M (next significant token is the configured `(`, matching `)` exists): `HS' = (hideset(name) ∩ hideset(closeParen)) ∪ {M}` (the Prosser intersection — `collectArgs` surfaces the close paren's hide set; an argument's own accreted hide set is UNIONED with `HS'`, never dropped). The cycle-2/3 cross-boundary witnesses were FLIPPED: `#define A(x) x`+`#define F(x) ((x)+100)`+`A(F)(3)` → `((3)+100)` (was the literal `F(3)`); `#define NAME SQ`+`#define SQ(x) ((x)*(x))`+`NAME(4)` → `((4)*(4))` (was a frozen bare `SQ`). PRESERVED: direct object/function self-reference freeze (`#define X X`→`X`; `#define F(x) F(x)`+`F(1)`→`F(1)`), mutual recursion termination (`P↔Q`+`P(1)`), nested/argument-pre-expansion, variadic, object — all unchanged. The `depth` backstop is RETAINED as defense-in-depth but now bounds NESTING (argument pre-expansion) rather than chain length: a finite object CHAIN (`M0`→…→`M300`→0) now expands ITERATIVELY in one frame to `0` (the cycle-2/3 `DeepMacroExpansionFailsLoudNotSilent` premise was a recursive-engine artifact — FLIPPED to `DeepFiniteMacroChainExpandsToValue`), while a pathological 256-deep-nested argument (`F(F(…F(0)…))`) still FAILS LOUD (`DeepNestedMacroArgumentFailsLoudNotSilent`). AGNOSTIC: the new machinery operates on `Token`/`SchemaTokenId` + macro NAMES only; `(`/`)`/`,`/`...`/`__VA_ARGS__` remain config-driven (no new hard-coded lexeme/arch/format string). +6 net preprocessor unit tests (2 cross-boundary FLIPs, 4 preserved-freeze) + reframed deep-chain (1→2) + runnable 4-target corpus `examples/c-subset/preprocessor_hideset` (object-macro-names-function-macro + function-returns-function-name, runtime-seeded via `ident`, exit 42). 333 ctest; all object/function/variadic preprocessor tests + corpora unregressed; RED-on-disable demonstrated (reverting object-like to isolated recursion mis-freezes `NAME(4)` → bare `SQ`, `test_preprocessor.cpp` `HideSetObjectMacroNamingFunctionMacroExpands` fails). *(Original status, preserved:)* FC13 cycle 2 (2026-06-19): the function-like macro rescan uses a recursive blue-PAINT set (`expand`'s `painting` keyed on the macro NAME) — an APPROXIMATION of the precise per-token §6.10.3.4 hide-set. It is correct for the common DIRECT-invocation forms (a name immediately or near-adjacently invoked, self-reference freeze, nested/argument-as-macro pre-expansion — all pinned), but does NOT expand cases where a function-like name and its `(` are produced across SEPARATE expansion streams: `#define A(x) x` + `#define F(x) ((x)+100)` + `A(F)(3)` → the `A(F)` yields a bare `F`, and the trailing `(3)` is NOT re-paired with it, so the result is the literal `F(3)`; likewise `#define NAME SQ` + `#define SQ(x) ((x)*(x))` + `NAME(4)` freezes to bare `SQ` (the object expansion of `NAME` does not re-scan to collect `(4)`). These residual cases are a COMPLETENESS gap, NOT a silent miscompile: each FAILS LOUD downstream at the PARSER (verified: `got F` / `got SQ` — a bare function-like name with a stray `(…)` is a syntax error), never producing wrong code. `A(F)(3)` is the constructible loud-failure witness. Co-designed with FC15's `#`/`##` token-marker cluster (the precise per-token hide-set is the same machinery that tracks `#`/`##` placemarkers). Priority: **normal / trigger-gated** — closes with FC15, or sooner if a real corpus needs cross-stream re-pairing. | Replace the name-keyed blue-paint with a precise per-token hide-set (each replacement token carries the set of macro names disabled for it, per §6.10.3.4): a token's hide-set is the intersection of the invoked-macro's hide-set with the next-token's, plus the invoked macro; re-pairing of a function-like name with a `(` produced by a SEPARATE expansion then follows. Pin: `A(F)(3)` → `((3)+100)`; `NAME(4)` → `((4)*(4))`. Implement alongside the FC15 `#`/`##` placemarker tokens. | plan 23 FC13/FC15; `src/analysis/preprocess/preprocessor.cpp` `expand`/`painting`; witness `A(F)(3)` (today fails loud `got F` at the parser); FC15-area cluster (precise hide-set co-designed with `#`/`##`) |
